the Dutch East Indies">Governors-General of the Dutch East Indies</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a>, 1610\xe2\x80\x931800)</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Products</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">Spices</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LowyInstitute_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LowyInstitute-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porcelain" title="Porcelain">porcelain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metals" class="mw-redirect" title="Metals">metals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grain" title="Grain">grain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Soybeans">soybeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_industry" title="Sugar industry">sugarcane</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Shih_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shih-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tseng_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tseng-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_African_wine" title="South African wine">wine</a><sup id="cite_ref-Estreicher_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estreicher-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fourie&amp;vonFintel_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourie&amp;vonFintel-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Williams_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Dutch East India Company</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Vereenigde Oostindische Compagnie</i>; <b>VOC</b>) was an <a href="/wiki/Early_modern" class="mw-redirect" title="Early modern">early modern</a> <a href="/wiki/Megacorporation" title="Megacorporation">megacorporation</a>, founded by a <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Dutch Republic">government-directed</a> <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_(business)" title="Consolidation (business)">amalgamation</a> of several rival Dutch trading companies (the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn</a></i> or <i>pre-companies</i>) in the early 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Unoki_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unoki-15">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It was originally established, on 20 March 1602, as a <a href="/wiki/Chartered_company" title="Chartered company">chartered company</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dutch_India" title="Dutch India">trade with India</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indianized_kingdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Indianized kingdoms">Indianized</a> <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian countries</a> when the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">Dutch government</a> granted it a 21-year <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a> on the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a>. The VOC was an early <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational/transnational corporation</a> in its modern sense. The Company has been often labelled a <a href="/wiki/Trading_company" title="Trading company">trading company</a> (a company of <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchants</a>) or sometimes a <a href="/wiki/Shipping_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping company">shipping company</a>. However, the VOC was in fact a proto-<a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Conglomerate company">conglomerate company</a>, diversifying into multiple commercial and industrial activities such as <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a> (especially intra-Asian trade),<sup id="cite_ref-AtsushiOta_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtsushiOta-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> shipbuilding, production and trade of <a href="/wiki/Spice_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Spice Islands">East Indian spices</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LowyInstitute_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LowyInstitute-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Taiwan" title="Economic history of Taiwan">Formosan sugarcane</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Shih_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shih-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tseng_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tseng-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_African_wine" title="History of South African wine">South African wine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Estreicher_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estreicher-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fourie&amp;vonFintel_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourie&amp;vonFintel-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Williams_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The Company was also a transcontinental <a href="/wiki/Employer" class="mw-redirect" title="Employer">employer</a> and an early pioneer of outward <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> at the dawn of <a href="/wiki/Modern_capitalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern capitalism">modern capitalism</a>. The Company\'s investment projects helped raise the commercial and industrial potential of many underdeveloped or undeveloped regions of the world in the early modern period.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1600s, by widely issuing <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> to the general public,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> the VOC became the world\'s first formally <a href="/wiki/Listing_(finance)" title="Listing (finance)">listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> In other words, it was the first corporation to be ever actually listed on an official <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macaulay2015_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macaulay2015-32">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The VOC was influential in the rise of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">corporate-led globalization</a> in the early modern period. \n</p><p>With its pioneering institutional innovations and powerful roles in global business history, the Company is often considered by many to be the forerunner of modern corporations. In many respects, modern-day corporations are all the \'direct descendants\' of the VOC model.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RussellShorto_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussellShorto-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taylor,_Bryan_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor,_Bryan-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It was the VOC\'s 17th-century institutional innovations and business practices that laid the foundations for the rise of giant global corporations in subsequent centuries<sup id="cite_ref-Steensgaard_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steensgaard-38">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VonNordenflycht_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VonNordenflycht-40">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x94 as a highly significant and formidable socio-politico-economic force of the modern-day world<sup id="cite_ref-Upbin,_Bruce_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Upbin,_Bruce-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harlan_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlan-43">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wooldridge,_Adrian_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wooldridge,_Adrian-44">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LaFrance_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaFrance-45">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zahra_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahra-46">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x94 to become the dominant factor in almost all economic systems today, whether for better or worse.<sup id="cite_ref-AnupShah_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnupShah-47">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The VOC also served as the direct model for the organizational reconstruction of the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">English/British East India Company</a> (EIC) in 1657.<sup id="cite_ref-MurraySayle_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MurraySayle-48">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NiallFerguson2002_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NiallFerguson2002-49">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macaulay2015_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macaulay2015-32">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rajkamal2017_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajkamal2017-51">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The Company, for nearly 200 years of its existence (1602\xe2\x80\x931800), had effectively transformed itself from a corporate entity into a state, an empire, or even a world in its own right.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_works_about_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="List of works about the Dutch East India Company">One of the most influential and best expertly researched business enterprises in history</a>, the VOC\'s world has been the subject of a vast amount of literature, including works of fiction and non-fiction. \n</p><p>Dubbed the \'VOC Republic\' or \'VOC Empire\' by some,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> the Company was historically an exemplary (transcontinental) company-state<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;k&#93;</a></sup> rather than a pure <a href="/wiki/For-profit_corporation" title="For-profit corporation">for-profit corporation</a>. Originally a government-backed military-commercial enterprise, the VOC was the wartime brainchild of leading Dutch republican statesman <a href="/wiki/Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt" title="Johan van Oldenbarnevelt">Johan van Oldenbarnevelt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Dutch Republic">States-General</a>. From its inception in 1602, the Company was not only a commercial enterprise but also effectively an instrument of war in the young <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Dutch Republic\'s revolutionary global war</a> against the powerful <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> (1579\xe2\x80\x931648). In 1619, the Company forcibly established a central position in the Indonesian city of Jayakarta, changing the name to <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">modern-day Jakarta</a>). Over the next two centuries the Company acquired additional ports as trading bases and safeguarded their interests by taking over surrounding territory.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> To guarantee its supply it established positions in many countries and became an early pioneer of outward <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;l&#93;</a></sup> In its foreign colonies the VOC possessed quasi-governmental powers, including the ability to wage war, imprison and execute convicts,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> negotiate treaties, strike <a href="/wiki/Coinage_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Coinage of the Dutch East India Company">its own coins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dutch_East_India_Company_trading_posts_and_settlements" title="List of Dutch East India Company trading posts and settlements">establish colonies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> With increasing importance of foreign posts, the company is often considered the world\'s first true <a href="/wiki/Transnational_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnational corporation">transnational corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;m&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\nAlong with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> (WIC/GWIC), the VOC became seen as the international arm of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> and the symbolic power of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a>. To further its trade routes, the VOC-funded exploratory voyages such as those led by <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Duyfken" title="Duyfken">Duyfken</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> who revealed largely unknown landmasses to the western world. In the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Netherlandish_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography">Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography</a> (c. 1570s\xe2\x80\x931670s), VOC navigators and cartographers helped shape geographical knowledge of the modern world as we know them today.\n</p><p>Socio-economic changes in Europe, the shift in power balance, and less successful financial management resulted in a slow decline of the VOC between 1720 and 1799. After the financially disastrous <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Dutch War">Fourth Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1780\xe2\x80\x931784), the company was first nationalised in 1796,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and finally dissolved in 1799. All assets were taken over by the government with VOC territories becoming Dutch government colonies. \n</p><p>In spite of the VOC\'s historic roles and contributions, the Company has long been heavily criticized for its monopoly policy, <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">exploitation</a>, colonialism, uses of violence, and slavery.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" archives and records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#VOC_coinage"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">VOC coinage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#Notable_VOC_ships"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Notable VOC ships</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#Field_of_VOC_World_studies"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Field of VOC World studies</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-54"><a href="#VOC_World_archaeology"><span class="tocnumber">17.1</span> <span class="toctext">VOC World archaeology</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-55"><a href="#VOC_timeline_and_historical_firsts"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">VOC timeline and historical firsts</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-56"><a href="#Proto-VOC_period_(with_the_establishment_of_the_voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)"><span class="tocnumber">18.1</span> <span class="toctext">Proto-VOC period (with the establishment of the <i>voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</i>)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-57"><a href="#VOC_era_(with_the_amalgamation_of_the_voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)"><span class="tocnumber">18.2</span> <span class="toctext">VOC era (with the amalgamation of the <i>voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</i>)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-58"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-59"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">20</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-60"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">21</span> <span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-62"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">23</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-63"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">24</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span id="Company_name.2C_logo.2C_and_flag"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_name,_logo,_and_flag">Company name, logo, and flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Company name, logo, and flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/East_India" title="East India">Colonial Indian companies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_India" title="Colonial India">Colonial India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Greater India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Colonial_Indian_companies" title="Category:Colonial Indian companies">Category:Colonial Indian companies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/East_Indiaman" title="East Indiaman">East Indiaman</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG/170px-Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG" width="170" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG/255px-Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG/340px-Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5123" data-file-height="3445" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heraldy_at_the_Castle_of_Good_Hope.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In terms of creating and sustaining an effective <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Corporate_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate culture">corporate culture</a>), the United East India Company (VOC) was a successful early pioneer at the dawn of modern capitalism.<sup id="cite_ref-GavinLucas(2006)_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GavinLucas(2006)-69">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_(VOC),_Hoorn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg/300px-17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg/450px-17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg/600px-17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_%28VOC%29%2C_Hoorn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3088" data-file-height="2056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:17th_century_plaque_to_Dutch_East_India_Company_(VOC),_Hoorn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>17th century plaque to Dutch East India Company (VOC), <a href="/wiki/Hoorn" title="Hoorn">Hoorn</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC-Amsterdam.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/VOC-Amsterdam.svg/170px-VOC-Amsterdam.svg.png" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/VOC-Amsterdam.svg/255px-VOC-Amsterdam.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/VOC-Amsterdam.svg/340px-VOC-Amsterdam.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="149" data-file-height="207" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC-Amsterdam.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo of the Amsterdam Chamber of the VOC</div></div></div>\n<p>In Dutch the name of the company is <i>Vereenigde Oostindische Compagnie</i> or <i>Verenigde Oost-Indische Compagnie</i>. abbreviated to <i>VOC</i>.\nThe company\'s <a href="/wiki/Monogram" title="Monogram">monogram</a> logo was possibly in fact the first globally recognized <a href="/wiki/Corporate_logo" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate logo">corporate logo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The logo of the VOC consisted of a large <a href="/wiki/Capital_letter" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital letter">capital</a> \'V\' with an O on the left and a C on the right leg. It appeared on various corporate items, such as <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannons</a> and coins. The first letter of the hometown of the chamber conducting the operation was placed on top (see figure for example of the Amsterdam Chamber logo). The monogram, versatility, flexibility, clarity, simplicity, symmetry, timelessness, and symbolism are considered notable characteristics of the VOC\'s professionally designed logo, those ensured its success at a time when the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a> was virtually unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GavinLucas(2006)_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GavinLucas(2006)-69">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> An Australian <a href="/wiki/Vintner" class="mw-redirect" title="Vintner">vintner</a> has used the VOC logo since the late 20th century, having re-registered the company\'s name for the purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\nThe flag of the company was red, white, and blue (see <a href="/wiki/Dutch_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch flag">Dutch flag</a>), with the company logo embroidered on it.\n</p><p>Around the world and especially in English-speaking countries, the VOC is widely known as the "Dutch East India Company". The name \xe2\x80\x98Dutch East India Company\xe2\x80\x99 is used to make a distinction with the [British] <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> (EIC) and <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="East India Company (disambiguation)">other East Indian companies</a> (such as the <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Danish East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_East_India_Company" title="Portuguese East India Company">Portuguese East India Company</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">Swedish East India Company</a>). The company\'s alternative names that have been used include the \'Dutch East Indies Company\', \'United East India Company\', \'United East Indian Company\', \'United East Indies Company\', \'Jan Company\', or \'Jan Compagnie\'.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="First Dutch Expedition to Indonesia">First Dutch Expedition to Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Second_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Dutch Expedition to Indonesia">Second Dutch Expedition to Indonesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">Voorcompagnie</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">Spice trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Route" title="Cape Route">Cape Route</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg/200px-Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg" width="200" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg/300px-Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg/400px-Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2093" data-file-height="2668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michiel_Jansz_van_Mierevelt_-_Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "United East Indian Company", or "United East Indies Company" (also known by the abbreviation "VOC" in Dutch) was the brainchild of <a href="/wiki/Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt" title="Johan van Oldenbarnevelt">Johan van Oldenbarnevelt</a>, the leading statesman of the Dutch Republic.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>, Antwerp had played an important role as a distribution centre in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">northern Europe</a>. After 1591, however, the Portuguese used an international syndicate of the German <a href="/wiki/Fugger" title="Fugger">Fuggers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welser" title="Welser">Welsers</a>, and Spanish and Italian firms, that used Hamburg as the northern staple port to distribute their goods, thereby cutting Dutch merchants out of the trade. At the same time, the Portuguese trade system was unable to increase supply to satisfy growing demand, in particular the demand for pepper. Demand for spices was relatively <a href="/wiki/Price_elasticity_of_demand" title="Price elasticity of demand">inelastic</a>, and therefore each lag in the supply of pepper caused a sharp rise in pepper prices.\n</p><p>In 1580 the Portuguese crown was <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">united</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with the Spanish crown, with which the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> was at war. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> therefore became an appropriate target for Dutch military incursions. These factors motivated Dutch merchants to enter the intercontinental spice trade themselves. Further, a number of Dutchmen like <a href="/wiki/Jan_Huyghen_van_Linschoten" title="Jan Huyghen van Linschoten">Jan Huyghen van Linschoten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_de_Houtman" title="Cornelis de Houtman">Cornelis de Houtman</a> obtained first hand knowledge of the "secret" Portuguese trade routes and practices, thereby providing opportunity.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oih1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Oih1.jpg/220px-Oih1.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Oih1.jpg/330px-Oih1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Oih1.jpg/440px-Oih1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oih1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oost-Indisch_Huis" title="Oost-Indisch Huis">VOC headquarters</a> in Amsterdam</div></div></div>\n<p>The stage was thus set for the four-ship exploratory expedition by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_de_Houtman" title="Frederick de Houtman">Frederick de Houtman</a> in 1595 to <a href="/wiki/Bantam_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantam (city)">Banten</a>, the main pepper port of West Java, where they clashed with both the Portuguese and indigenous Indonesians. Houtman\'s expedition then sailed east along the north coast of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, losing twelve crew to a Javanese attack at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sidayu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sidayu (page does not exist)">Sidayu</a> and killing a local ruler in <a href="/wiki/Madura" class="mw-redirect" title="Madura">Madura</a>. Half the crew were lost before the expedition made it back to the Netherlands the following year, but with enough spices to make a considerable profit.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp27_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp27-75">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg/200px-ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg" width="200" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg/300px-ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg/400px-ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg 2x" data-file-width="837" data-file-height="386" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ThuiskomstVanNeck1599.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Return of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Dutch Expedition to Indonesia">second Asia expedition</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Neck" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacob van Neck">Jacob van Neck</a> in 1599 by <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_Vroom" title="Cornelis Vroom">Cornelis Vroom</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1598, an increasing number of fleets were sent out by competing merchant groups from around the Netherlands. Some fleets were lost, but most were successful, with some voyages producing high profits. In March 1599, a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Second_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia_(1598%E2%80%931600)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Second Dutch Expedition to Indonesia (1598\xe2\x80\x931600) (page does not exist)">fleet of eight ships</a> under <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Neck" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacob van Neck">Jacob van Neck</a> was the first Dutch fleet to reach the \'Spice Islands\' of Maluku, the source of pepper, cutting out the Javanese middlemen. The ships returned to Europe in 1599 and 1600 and the expedition made a 400 percent profit.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp27_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp27-75">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1600, the Dutch joined forces with the Muslim Hituese on <a href="/wiki/Ambon_Island" title="Ambon Island">Ambon Island</a> in an anti-Portuguese alliance, in return for which the Dutch were given the sole right to purchase spices from Hitu.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp28_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp28-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Dutch control of Ambon was achieved when the Portuguese surrendered their fort in Ambon to the Dutch-Hituese alliance. In 1613, the Dutch expelled the Portuguese from their <a href="/wiki/Solor" title="Solor">Solor</a> fort, but a subsequent Portuguese attack led to a second change of hands; following this second reoccupation, the Dutch once again captured Solor, in 1636.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp28_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp28-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>East of Solor, on the island of Timor, Dutch advances were halted by an autonomous and powerful group of Portuguese Eurasians called the <a href="/wiki/Topasses" title="Topasses">Topasses</a>. They remained in control of the <a href="/wiki/Sandalwood" title="Sandalwood">Sandalwood</a> trade and their resistance lasted throughout the 17th and 18th centuries, causing <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> to remain under the Portuguese sphere of control.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Formation.2C_rise.2C_and_fall"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation,_rise,_and_fall">Formation, rise, and fall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Formation, rise, and fall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:History_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:History of the Dutch East India Company">History of the Dutch East India Company (VOC)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Dutch_Empire" title="Evolution of the Dutch Empire">Evolution of the Dutch Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company_in_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch East India Company in Indonesia">Dutch East India Company in Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic history of the Dutch Republic">Economic history of the Dutch Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Financial_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Financial history of the Dutch Republic">Financial history of the Dutch Republic</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formative_years">Formative years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Formative years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Reproductie_van_een_plattegrond_van_Batavia_uit_circa_1627_TMnr_496-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reproduction of a map of the city of Batavia c.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1627, collection <a href="/wiki/Tropenmuseum" title="Tropenmuseum">Tropenmuseum</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg/220px-Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg/330px-Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg/440px-Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4712" data-file-height="3720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waere_affbeeldinge_Wegens_het_Casteel_ende_Stadt_BATAVIA_gelegen_opt_groot_Eylant_JAVA_Anno_1681.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch Batavia in 1681, built in what is now <a href="/wiki/North_Jakarta" title="North Jakarta">North Jakarta</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At the time, it was customary for a company to be set up only for the duration of a single voyage and to be liquidated upon the return of the fleet. Investment in these expeditions was a very high-risk venture, not only because of the usual dangers of piracy, disease and shipwreck, but also because the interplay of inelastic demand and relatively elastic supply<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> of spices could make prices tumble at just the wrong moment, thereby ruining prospects of profitability. To manage such risk the forming of a <a href="/wiki/Cartel" title="Cartel">cartel</a> to control supply would seem logical. The English had been the first to adopt this approach, by bundling their resources into a <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a> enterprise, the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">English East India Company</a> in 1600, thereby threatening their Dutch competitors with ruin.<sup id="cite_ref-Woude_p._384\xe2\x80\x93385_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woude_p._384\xe2\x80\x93385-80">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1602, the Dutch government followed suit, sponsoring the creation of a single "United East Indies Company" that was also granted monopoly over the Asian trade. For a time in the seventeenth century, they were able to monopolize the trade in nutmeg, mace, and cloves and to sell these spices in Europe and India at fourteen to seventeen times the price they paid in Indonesia;<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> while Dutch profits soared, the local economy of the Spice Islands was destroyed. With a capital of 6,440,200 <a href="/wiki/Guilder" title="Guilder">guilders</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> the charter of the new company empowered it to build forts, maintain armies, and conclude treaties with Asian rulers. It provided for a venture that would continue for 21 years, with a financial accounting only at the end of each decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Woude_p._384\xe2\x80\x93385_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Woude_p._384\xe2\x80\x93385-80">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 1603, the Company seized the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(ship)" title="Santa Catarina (ship)"><i>Santa Catarina</i></a>, a 1500-ton Portuguese merchant <a href="/wiki/Carrack" title="Carrack">carrack</a>, off the coast of Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> She was such a rich prize that her sale proceeds increased the capital of the VOC by more than 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-boyajian_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boyajian-84">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in 1603 the first permanent Dutch trading post in Indonesia was established in <a href="/wiki/Banten" title="Banten">Banten</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>, and in 1611 another was established at <a href="/wiki/Jayakarta" class="mw-redirect" title="Jayakarta">Jayakarta</a> (later "Batavia" and then "Jakarta").<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp29_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp29-85">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In 1610, the VOC established the post of <a href="/wiki/Governor_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor General">Governor General</a> to more firmly control their affairs in Asia. To advise and control the risk of <a href="/wiki/Despotism" title="Despotism">despotic</a> Governors General, a Council of the Indies (<i>Raad van Indi\xc3\xab</i>) was created. The Governor General effectively became the main administrator of the VOC\'s activities in Asia, although the <i>Heeren XVII</i>, a body of 17 shareholders representing different chambers, continued to officially have overall control.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp28_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp28-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amboina._17th_century_print,_most_likely_English..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg/220px-Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg/330px-Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg/440px-Amboina._17th_century_print%2C_most_likely_English..jpg 2x" data-file-width="1212" data-file-height="918" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amboina._17th_century_print,_most_likely_English..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Isle of Amboina</i>, a 17th-century print, probably English</div></div></div>\n<p>VOC headquarters were located in <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Ambon" title="Governorate of Ambon">Ambon</a> during the tenures of the first three Governors General (1610\xe2\x80\x931619), but it was not a satisfactory location. Although it was at the centre of the spice production areas, it was far from the Asian trade routes and other VOC areas of activity ranging from Africa to India to Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> A location in the west of the archipelago was thus sought. The Straits of Malacca were strategic but had become dangerous following the Portuguese conquest, and the first permanent VOC settlement in Banten was controlled by a powerful local ruler and subject to stiff competition from Chinese and English traders.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp28_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp28-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1604, a second English <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> voyage commanded by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Henry_Middleton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Henry Middleton">Sir Henry Middleton</a> reached the islands of <a href="/wiki/Ternate" title="Ternate">Ternate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tidore" title="Tidore">Tidore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambon_Island" title="Ambon Island">Ambon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">Banda</a>. In Banda, they encountered severe VOC hostility, sparking Anglo-Dutch competition for access to spices.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp29_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp29-85">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> From 1611 to 1617, the English established trading posts at <a href="/wiki/Sukadana" title="Sukadana">Sukadana</a> (southwest <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Makassar" title="Makassar">Makassar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jayakarta" class="mw-redirect" title="Jayakarta">Jayakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jepara" title="Jepara">Jepara</a> in <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, and Aceh, <a href="/wiki/Pariaman" title="Pariaman">Pariaman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jambi" title="Jambi">Jambi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, which threatened Dutch ambitions for a monopoly on East Indies trade.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp29_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp29-85">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Diplomatic agreements in Europe in 1620 ushered in a period of co-operation between the Dutch and the English over the spice trade.<sup id="cite_ref-RICKLEFSp29_85-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RICKLEFSp29-85">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> This ended with a notorious but disputed incident known as the \'<a href="/wiki/Amboyna_massacre" title="Amboyna massacre">Amboyna massacre</a>\', where ten Englishmen were arrested, tried and beheaded for conspiracy against the Dutch government.<sup id="cite_ref-MILLER_XVI_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MILLER_XVI-88">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Although this caused outrage in Europe and a diplomatic crisis, the English quietly withdrew from most of their Indonesian activities (except trading in Banten) and focused on other Asian interests.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth">Growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg/220px-Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg/330px-Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg/440px-Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Melaka-St-Paul-Dutch-graves-2182.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graves of Dutch dignitaries in the ruined <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Church,_Malacca" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul&#39;s Church, Malacca">St. Paul\'s Church, Malacca</a>, in the former <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malacca" title="Dutch Malacca">Dutch Malacca</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg/220px-De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg/330px-De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg/440px-De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1594" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_handelsloge_van_de_VOC_in_Hougly_in_Bengalen_Rijksmuseum_SK-A-4282.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Trade lodge of the VOC in Hooghly, Bengal</i>, by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hendrik_van_Schuylenburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hendrik van Schuylenburgh (page does not exist)">Hendrik van Schuylenburgh</a>, 1665</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1619, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieterszoon_Coen" title="Jan Pieterszoon Coen">Jan Pieterszoon Coen</a> was appointed Governor-General of the VOC. He saw the possibility of the VOC becoming an Asian power, both political and economic. On 30 May 1619, Coen, backed by a force of nineteen ships, stormed Jayakarta, driving out the Banten forces; and from the ashes established <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> as the VOC headquarters. In the 1620s almost the entire native population of the <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">Banda Islands</a> was driven away, starved to death, or killed in an attempt to replace them with Dutch plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> These plantations were used to grow <a href="/wiki/Cloves" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloves">cloves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> for export. Coen hoped to settle large numbers of Dutch colonists in the East Indies, but implementation of this policy never materialised, mainly because very few Dutch were willing to emigrate to Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another of Coen\'s ventures was more successful. A major problem in the European trade with Asia at the time was that the Europeans could offer few goods that Asian consumers wanted, except silver and gold. European traders therefore had to pay for spices with the precious metals, which were in short supply in Europe, except for Spain and Portugal. The Dutch and English had to obtain it by creating a trade surplus with other European countries. Coen discovered the obvious solution for the problem: to start an intra-Asiatic trade system, whose profits could be used to finance the spice trade with Europe. In the long run this obviated the need for exports of precious metals from Europe, though at first it required the formation of a large trading-capital fund in the Indies. The VOC reinvested a large share of its profits to this end in the period up to 1630.<sup id="cite_ref-vries386_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vries386-91">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The VOC traded throughout Asia. Ships coming into Batavia from the Netherlands carried supplies for VOC settlements in Asia. Silver and copper from Japan were used to trade with India and China for silk, cotton, porcelain, and textiles. These products were either traded within Asia for the coveted spices or brought back to Europe. The VOC was also instrumental in introducing European ideas and technology to Asia. The Company supported Christian missionaries and traded modern technology with China and Japan. A more peaceful VOC trade post on <a href="/wiki/Dejima" title="Dejima">Dejima</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_island" title="Artificial island">artificial island</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki,_Nagasaki" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagasaki, Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>, was for more than two hundred years the only place where Europeans were permitted to trade with Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> When the VOC tried to use military force to make <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> China open up to Dutch trade, the Chinese defeated the Dutch in <a href="/wiki/Sino%E2%80%93Dutch_conflicts" class="mw-redirect" title="Sino\xe2\x80\x93Dutch conflicts">a war over the Penghu islands</a> from 1623 to 1624, forcing the VOC to abandon <a href="/wiki/Penghu" title="Penghu">Penghu</a> for Taiwan. The Chinese defeated the VOC again at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Liaoluo_Bay" title="Battle of Liaoluo Bay">Battle of Liaoluo Bay</a> in 1633.\n</p><p>The Vietnamese Nguyen Lords defeated the VOC in <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BB%8Bnh%E2%80%93Nguy%E1%BB%85n_War#Later_campaigns" title="Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War">a 1643 battle</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BB%8Bnh%E2%80%93Nguy%E1%BB%85n_War" title="Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War">Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War</a>, blowing up a Dutch ship. The Cambodians defeated the VOC in the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Dutch_War" title="Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War">Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War</a> from 1643 to 1644 on the Mekong River.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg/220px-Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg/330px-Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg/440px-Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg 2x" data-file-width="918" data-file-height="712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_factory_at_Hooghly-Chinsura_1721.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch factory of Hugly\xe2\x80\x93Chinsurah in Bengal</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1640, the VOC obtained the port of <a href="/wiki/Galle" title="Galle">Galle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Ceylon</a>, from the Portuguese and broke the latter\'s monopoly of the <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a> trade. In 1658, <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Pietersz._Hulft" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerard Pietersz. Hulft">Gerard Pietersz. Hulft</a> laid siege to <a href="/wiki/Colombo" title="Colombo">Colombo</a>, which was captured with the help of King <a href="/wiki/Rajasinghe_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajasinghe II">Rajasinghe II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kandy" title="Kandy">Kandy</a>. By 1659, the Portuguese had been expelled from the coastal regions, which were then occupied by the VOC, securing for it the monopoly over cinnamon.\nTo prevent the Portuguese or the English from ever recapturing Sri Lanka, the VOC went on to conquer the entire <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malabar" title="Dutch Malabar">Malabar Coast</a> from the Portuguese, almost entirely driving them from the west coast of India. When news of a peace agreement between Portugal and the Netherlands reached Asia in 1663, Goa was the only remaining Portuguese city on the west coast.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1652, <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a> established an outpost at the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> (the southwestern tip of Africa, now <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, South Africa) to re-supply VOC ships on their journey to East Asia. This post later became a full-fledged colony, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, when more Dutch and other Europeans started to settle there.\n</p><p>Through the seventeenth century VOC trading posts were also established in <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Bengal" title="Dutch Bengal">Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malacca" title="Dutch Malacca">Malacca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Siam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Formosa</a> (now Taiwan), as well as the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malabar" title="Dutch Malabar">Malabar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Coromandel" title="Dutch Coromandel">Coromandel</a> coasts in India. Direct access to mainland China came in 1729 when a factory was established in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In 1662, however, <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> expelled the Dutch from Taiwan<sup id="cite_ref-Andrade_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andrade-95">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> (<i>see</i> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Taiwan" title="History of Taiwan">History of Taiwan</a>).\n</p><p>In 1663, the VOC signed the "Painan Treaty" with several local lords in the <a href="/wiki/Painan" title="Painan">Painan</a> area that were revolting against the <a href="/wiki/Aceh_Sultanate" title="Aceh Sultanate">Aceh Sultanate</a>. The treaty allowed the VOC to build a trading post in the area and eventually to monopolise the trade there, especially the <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> trade.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1669, the VOC was the richest private company the world had ever seen, with over 150 merchant ships, 40 warships, 50,000 employees, a private army of 10,000 soldiers, and a <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividend</a> payment of 40% on the original investment.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-97">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many of the VOC employees inter-mixed with the indigenous peoples and expanded the population of <a href="/wiki/Indos_in_pre-colonial_history" title="Indos in pre-colonial history">Indos in pre-colonial history</a> <sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reorientation">Reorientation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reorientation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="background:#f8eaba; text-align:center;"><b>Reorientation</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG/80px-East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG" width="80" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG/120px-East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG/160px-East_Indies_Company_sword-J_09842-IMG_0919.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2836" data-file-height="4254" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Sword of the East India Company, featuring the V.O.C. monogram of the guard. /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>This <a href="/wiki/Kraak_porcelain" class="mw-redirect" title="Kraak porcelain">Kraak porcelain</a> dish (in a museum in <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>) was emblazoned with the <a href="/wiki/Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie" class="mw-redirect" title="Vereenigde Oostindische Compagnie">V.O.C.</a> <a href="/wiki/Monogram" title="Monogram">monogram</a>.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:31px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC_Octrooigebied_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
