//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/VOC_Octrooigebied_1.jpg/240px-VOC_Octrooigebied_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1659" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Trade area of the VOC around 1700 CE.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:29.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg/120px-Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg" width="120" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg/180px-Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg/240px-Dutch_VOC_ships_in_Chittagong_or_Arakan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="368" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>VOC ships in <a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a> or <a href="/wiki/Arakan" title="Arakan">Arakan</a>.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:26px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/120px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg" width="120" height="98" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/180px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/240px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1951" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>City hall of Batavia in 1682 CE.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_(1663).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg/96px-Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg" width="96" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg/144px-Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg/192px-Natives_of_Arrakan_sell_slaves_to_the_Dutch_East_India_Company_%281663%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="955" data-file-height="1194" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Natives of <a href="/wiki/Rakhine_State" title="Rakhine State">Arakan</a> sell slaves to the Dutch East India Company, c.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1663 CE.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Around 1670, two events caused the growth of VOC trade to stall. In the first place, the highly profitable trade with Japan started to decline. The loss of the outpost on Formosa to <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> in the 1662 <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Zeelandia" title="Siege of Fort Zeelandia">Siege of Fort Zeelandia</a> and related internal turmoil in China (where the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> was being replaced with the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing dynasty</a>) brought an end to the silk trade after 1666. Though the VOC substituted Bengali for Chinese silk other forces affected the supply of Japanese silver and gold. The <a href="/wiki/Shogunate" class="mw-redirect" title="Shogunate">shogunate</a> enacted a number of measures to limit the export of these precious metals, in the process limiting VOC opportunities for trade, and severely worsening the terms of trade. Therefore, Japan ceased to function as the lynchpin of the intra-Asiatic trade of the VOC by 1685.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Even more importantly, the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a> temporarily interrupted VOC trade with Europe. This caused a spike in the price of pepper, which enticed the English East India Company (EIC) to enter this market aggressively in the years after 1672. Previously, one of the tenets of the VOC pricing policy was to slightly over-supply the pepper market, so as to depress prices below the level where interlopers were encouraged to enter the market (instead of striving for short-term profit maximisation). The wisdom of such a policy was illustrated when a fierce price war with the EIC ensued, as that company flooded the market with new supplies from India. In this struggle for market share, the VOC (which had much larger financial resources) could wait out the EIC. Indeed, by 1683, the latter came close to bankruptcy; its share price plummeted from 600 to 250; and its president <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Child" title="Josiah Child">Josiah Child</a> was temporarily forced from office.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, the writing was on the wall. Other companies, like the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Danish East India Company</a> also started to make inroads on the Dutch system. The VOC therefore closed the heretofore flourishing open pepper emporium of <a href="/wiki/Bantam_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantam (city)">Bantam</a> by a treaty of 1684 with the Sultan. Also, on the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Coromandel" title="Dutch Coromandel">Coromandel Coast</a>, it moved its chief stronghold from <a href="/wiki/Pulicat" title="Pulicat">Pulicat</a> to <a href="/wiki/Negapatnam" class="mw-redirect" title="Negapatnam">Negapatnam</a>, so as to secure a monopoly on the pepper trade at the detriment of the French and the Danes.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> However, the importance of these traditional commodities in the Asian-European trade was diminishing rapidly at the time. The military outlays that the VOC needed to make to enhance its monopoly were not justified by the increased profits of this declining trade.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nevertheless, this lesson was slow to sink in and at first the VOC made the strategic decision to improve its military position on the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malabar" title="Dutch Malabar">Malabar Coast</a> (hoping thereby to curtail English influence in the area, and end the drain on its resources from the cost of the Malabar garrisons) by using force to compel the <a href="/wiki/Saamoothiri" class="mw-redirect" title="Saamoothiri">Zamorin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kozhikode" title="Kozhikode">Calicut</a> to submit to Dutch domination. In 1710, the Zamorin was made to sign a treaty with the VOC undertaking to trade exclusively with the VOC and expel other European traders. For a brief time, this appeared to improve the Company\'s prospects. However, in 1715, with EIC encouragement, the Zamorin renounced the treaty. Though a Dutch army managed to suppress this insurrection temporarily, the Zamorin continued to trade with the English and the French, which led to an appreciable upsurge in English and French traffic. The VOC decided in 1721 that it was no longer worth the trouble to try to dominate the <a href="/wiki/Malabar_pepper" title="Malabar pepper">Malabar pepper</a> and spice trade. A strategic decision was taken to scale down the Dutch military presence and in effect yield the area to EIC influence.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/250px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/375px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG/500px-De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Lannoy_Surrender.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eustachius_De_Lannoy" title="Eustachius De Lannoy">Eustachius De Lannoy</a> of the Dutch East India Company surrenders to Maharaja <a href="/wiki/Marthanda_Varma" title="Marthanda Varma">Marthanda Varma</a> of the <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Travancore" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Travancore">Kingdom of Travancore</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Colachel" title="Battle of Colachel">Battle of Colachel</a>. (Depiction at <a href="/wiki/Padmanabhapuram_Palace" title="Padmanabhapuram Palace">Padmanabhapuram Palace</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>The 1741 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Colachel" title="Battle of Colachel">Battle of Colachel</a> by  warriors of <a href="/wiki/Travancore" title="Travancore">Travancore</a> under Raja <a href="/wiki/Marthanda_Varma" title="Marthanda Varma">Marthanda Varma</a> defeated the Dutch. The Dutch commander Captain <a href="/wiki/Eustachius_De_Lannoy" title="Eustachius De Lannoy">Eustachius De Lannoy</a> was captured. Marthanda Varma agreed to spare the Dutch captain\'s life on condition that he joined his army and trained his soldiers on modern lines. This defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Travancore-Dutch_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Travancore-Dutch War">Travancore-Dutch War</a> is considered the earliest example of an organised Asian power overcoming European military technology and tactics; and it signalled the decline of Dutch power in India.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The attempt to continue as before as a low volume-high profit business enterprise with its core business in the spice trade had therefore failed. The Company had however already (reluctantly) followed the example of its European competitors in diversifying into other Asian commodities, like tea, coffee, cotton, textiles, and sugar. These commodities provided a lower profit margin and therefore required a larger sales volume to generate the same amount of revenue. This structural change in the commodity composition of the VOC\'s trade started in the early 1680s, after the temporary collapse of the EIC around 1683 offered an excellent opportunity to enter these markets. The actual cause for the change lies, however, in two structural features of this new era.\n</p><p>In the first place, there was a revolutionary change in the tastes affecting European demand for Asian textiles, coffee and tea, around the turn of the 18th century. Secondly, a new era of an abundant supply of capital at low interest rates suddenly opened around this time. The second factor enabled the Company easily to finance its expansion in the new areas of commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Between the 1680s and 1720s, the VOC was therefore able to equip and man an appreciable expansion of its fleet, and acquire a large amount of precious metals to finance the purchase of large amounts of Asian commodities, for shipment to Europe. The overall effect was approximately to double the size of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The tonnage of the returning ships rose by 125 percent in this period. However, the Company\'s revenues from the sale of goods landed in Europe rose by only 78 percent. This reflects the basic change in the VOC\'s circumstances that had occurred: it now operated in new markets for goods with an elastic demand, in which it had to compete on an equal footing with other suppliers. This made for low profit margins.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Unfortunately, the business information systems of the time made this difficult to discern for the managers of the company, which may partly explain the mistakes they made from hindsight. This lack of information might have been counteracted (as in earlier times in the VOC\'s history) by the business acumen of the directors. Unfortunately by this time these were almost exclusively recruited from the political <i><a href="/wiki/Regenten" title="Regenten">regent</a></i> class, which had long since lost its close relationship with merchant circles.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Low profit margins in themselves do not explain the deterioration of revenues. To a large extent the costs of the operation of the VOC had a "fixed" character (military establishments; maintenance of the fleet and such). Profit levels might therefore have been maintained if the increase in the scale of trading operations that in fact took place had resulted in <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a>. However, though larger ships transported the growing volume of goods, labour productivity did not go up sufficiently to realise these. In general the Company\'s overhead rose in step with the growth in trade volume; declining gross margins translated directly into a decline in profitability of the invested capital. The era of expansion was one of "profitless growth".<sup id="cite_ref-De_Vries_and_Van_der_Woude,_p._447_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Vries_and_Van_der_Woude,_p._447-110">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Specifically:  "[t]he long-term average annual profit in the VOC\'s 1630\xe2\x80\x9370 \'Golden Age\' was 2.1 million guilders, of which just under half was distributed as dividends and the remainder reinvested. The long-term average annual profit in the \'Expansion Age\' (1680\xe2\x80\x931730) was 2.0 million guilders, of which three-quarters was distributed as dividend and one-quarter reinvested. In the earlier period, profits averaged 18 percent of total revenues; in the latter period, 10 percent. The annual return of invested capital in the earlier period stood at approximately 6 percent; in the latter period, 3.4 percent."<sup id="cite_ref-De_Vries_and_Van_der_Woude,_p._447_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Vries_and_Van_der_Woude,_p._447-110">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nevertheless, in the eyes of investors the VOC did not do too badly. The share price hovered consistently around the 400 mark from the mid-1680s (excepting a hiccup around the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> in 1688), and they reached an all-time high of around 642 in the 1720s. VOC shares then yielded a return of 3.5 percent, only slightly less than the yield on Dutch government bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_and_fall">Decline and fall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Decline and fall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(March 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>After 1730, the fortunes of the VOC started to decline. Five major problems, not all of equal weight, explain its decline over the next fifty years to 1780:<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>There was a steady erosion of intra-Asiatic trade because of changes in the Asiatic political and economic environment that the VOC could do little about. These factors gradually squeezed the company out of Persia, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Suratte" title="Dutch Suratte">Suratte</a>, the Malabar Coast, and Bengal. The company had to confine its operations to the belt it physically controlled, from Ceylon through the Indonesian archipelago. The volume of this intra-Asiatic trade, and its profitability, therefore had to shrink.</li>\n<li>The way the company was organised in Asia (centralised on its hub in Batavia), that initially had offered advantages in gathering market information, began to cause disadvantages in the 18th century because of the inefficiency of first shipping everything to this central point. This disadvantage was most keenly felt in the tea trade, where competitors like the EIC and the <a href="/wiki/Ostend_Company" title="Ostend Company">Ostend Company</a> shipped directly from China to Europe.</li>\n<li>The "venality" of the VOC\'s personnel (in the sense of corruption and non-performance of duties), though a problem for all East India Companies at the time, seems to have plagued the VOC on a larger scale than its competitors. To be sure, the company was not a "good employer". Salaries were low, and "private-account trading" was officially not allowed. Not surprisingly, it proliferated in the 18th century to the detriment of the company\'s performance.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> From about the 1790s onward, the phrase <i>perished under corruption</i> (<i>vergaan onder corruptie</i>, also abbreviated VOC in Dutch) came to summarise the company\'s future.</li>\n<li>A problem that the VOC shared with other companies was the high mortality and morbidity rates among its employees. This decimated the company\'s ranks and enervated many of the survivors.</li>\n<li>A self-inflicted wound was the VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Dividend_policy" title="Dividend policy">dividend policy</a>. The dividends distributed by the company had exceeded the surplus it garnered in Europe in every decade from 1690 to 1760 except 1710\xe2\x80\x931720. However, in the period up to 1730 the directors shipped resources to Asia to build up the trading capital there. Consolidated bookkeeping therefore probably would have shown that total profits exceeded dividends. In addition, between 1700 and 1740 the company retired 5.4&#160;million guilders of long-term debt. The company therefore was still on a secure financial footing in these years. This changed after 1730. While profits plummeted the <i>bewindhebbers</i> only slightly decreased dividends from the earlier level. Distributed dividends were therefore in excess of earnings in every decade but one (1760\xe2\x80\x931770). To accomplish this, the Asian capital stock had to be drawn down by 4&#160;million guilders between 1730 and 1780, and the <a href="/wiki/Market_liquidity" title="Market liquidity">liquid</a> capital available in Europe was reduced by 20 million guilders in the same period. The directors were therefore constrained to replenish the company\'s liquidity by resorting to short-term financing from anticipatory loans, backed by expected revenues from home-bound fleets.</li></ul>\n<p>Despite these problems, the VOC in 1780 remained an enormous operation. Its capital in the Republic, consisting of ships and goods in inventory, totalled 28&#160;million guilders; its capital in Asia, consisting of the liquid trading fund and goods en route to Europe, totalled 46&#160;million guilders. Total capital, net of outstanding debt, stood at 62 million guilders. The prospects of the company at this time therefore were not hopeless, had one of the plans for reform been undertaken successfully. However, the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Dutch War">Fourth Anglo-Dutch War</a> intervened. British attacks in Europe and Asia reduced the VOC fleet by half; removed valuable cargo from its control; and devastated its remaining power in Asia. The direct losses of the VOC can be calculated at 43&#160;million guilders. Loans to keep the company operating reduced its net assets to zero.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1720 on, the market for sugar from Indonesia declined as the competition from cheap sugar from Brazil increased. European markets became saturated. Dozens of Chinese sugar traders went bankrupt, which led to massive unemployment, which in turn led to gangs of unemployed <a href="/wiki/Coolies" class="mw-redirect" title="Coolies">coolies</a>. The Dutch government in Batavia did not adequately respond to these problems. In 1740, rumours of deportation of the gangs from the Batavia area led to widespread rioting. The Dutch military searched houses of Chinese in Batavia for weapons. When a house accidentally burnt down, military and impoverished citizens started slaughtering and pillaging the Chinese community.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/1740_Batavia_massacre" title="1740 Batavia massacre">massacre of the Chinese</a> was deemed sufficiently serious for the board of the VOC to start an official investigation into the Government of the Dutch East Indies for the first time in its history.\n</p><p>After the Fourth Anglo-Dutch War, the VOC was a financial wreck. After vain attempts at reorganisation by the provincial States of Holland and Zeeland, it was nationalised by the new <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a> on 1 March 1796.<sup id="cite_ref-tanap_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tanap-116">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The VOC charter was renewed several times, but was allowed to expire on 31 December 1799.<sup id="cite_ref-tanap_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tanap-116">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Most of the possessions of the former VOC were subsequently occupied by Great Britain during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic wars">Napoleonic wars</a>, but after the new <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> was created by the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, some of these were restored to this successor state of the Dutch Republic by the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Treaty_of_1814" title="Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1814">Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1814</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure">Organizational structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Organizational structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">The United East India Company (VOC) - a pioneering early model of the multinational/transnational corporation in its modern sense.</div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_(17e_eeuw).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg/200px-Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg" width="200" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg/300px-Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg/400px-Gravure_van_het_Oost_Indisch_Huis_%2817e_eeuw%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="562" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">17th-century etching of the <a href="/wiki/Oost-Indisch_Huis" title="Oost-Indisch Huis">Oost-Indisch Huis</a> (East India House), the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">global headquarters</a> of the VOC.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg/200px-Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg" width="200" height="142" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg/300px-Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg/400px-Andries_Beeckman_-_The_Castle_of_Batavia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7222" data-file-height="5134" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">It was in <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>) on the island of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> that the VOC <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company_in_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch East India Company in Indonesia">established its administrative center</a>, as the second headquarters, with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_the_Dutch_East_Indies" title="List of Governors-General of the Dutch East Indies">Governor-General</a> in charge from 1610 onwards. The company also had <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dutch_East_India_Company_trading_posts_and_settlements" title="List of Dutch East India Company trading posts and settlements">important operations elsewhere</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg/220px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg/330px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg/440px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bond</a> from the Dutch East India Company (VOC), dating from 7 November 1623. The VOC was the first company in history to issue <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> to the general public. It was the VOC that invented the idea of investing in the company rather than in a specific venture governed by the company. The VOC was also the first company to use a fully-fledged <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital market</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Bond_market" title="Bond market">bond market</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a>) as a crucial channel to raise medium-term and long-term funds.</div></div></div>\n<p>The VOC is generally considered to be the world\'s first truly <a href="/wiki/Transnational_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnational corporation">transnational corporation</a> and it was also the first <a href="/wiki/Multinational_enterprise" class="mw-redirect" title="Multinational enterprise">multinational enterprise</a> to issue <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> to the public. Some historians such as <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Brook" title="Timothy Brook">Timothy Brook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Shorto" title="Russell Shorto">Russell Shorto</a> consider the VOC as the pioneering <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a> in the first wave of the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">corporate globalization</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RussellShorto_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussellShorto-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The VOC was the first multinational corporation to operate officially in different <a href="/wiki/Continents" class="mw-redirect" title="Continents">continents</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. While the VOC mainly operated in what later became the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (modern Indonesia), the company also had important operations elsewhere. It employed people from different continents and origins in the same functions and working environments. Although it was a Dutch company its <a href="/wiki/Employee" class="mw-redirect" title="Employee">employees</a> included not only people from the Netherlands, but also many from Germany and from other countries as well. Besides the diverse north-west European <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a> recruited by the VOC in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, the VOC made extensive use of local Asian labour markets. As a result, the personnel of the various VOC offices in Asia consisted of European and Asian employees. Asian or <a href="/wiki/Eurasian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurasian">Eurasian</a> workers might be employed as sailors, soldiers, writers, carpenters, smiths, or as simple unskilled workers.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> At the height of its existence the VOC had 25,000 employees who worked in Asia and 11,000 who were en route.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Also, while most of its <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a> were Dutch, about a quarter of the initial shareholders were Zuid-Nederlanders (people from an area that includes modern Belgium and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>) and there were also a few dozen Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The VOC had two types of shareholders: the <i>participanten</i>, who could be seen as non-managing members, and the 76 <i>bewindhebbers</i> (later reduced to 60) who acted as managing directors. This was the usual set-up for Dutch <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock companies</a> at the time. The innovation in the case of the VOC was that the liability of not just the <i>participanten</i> but also of the <i>bewindhebbers</i> was limited to the paid-in capital (usually, <i>bewindhebbers</i> had unlimited liability). The VOC therefore was a <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited liability company</a>. Also, the capital would be <i>permanent</i> during the lifetime of the company. As a consequence, investors that wished to liquidate their interest in the interim could only do this by selling their share to others on the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Confusion_of_confusions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Confusion of confusions (page does not exist)">Confusion of confusions</a></i>, a 1688 dialogue by the Sephardi Jew <a href="/wiki/Joseph_de_la_Vega" title="Joseph de la Vega">Joseph de la Vega</a> analysed the workings of this one-stock exchange.\n</p><p>The VOC consisted of six Chambers (<i>Kamers</i>) in port cities: <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enkhuizen" title="Enkhuizen">Enkhuizen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middelburg" title="Middelburg">Middelburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hoorn" title="Hoorn">Hoorn</a>. Delegates of these chambers convened as the <i>Heeren XVII</i> (the Lords Seventeen). They were selected from the <i>bewindhebber</i>-class of shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the <i>Heeren XVII</i>, eight delegates were from the Chamber of Amsterdam (one short of a majority on its own), four from the Chamber of Zeeland, and one from each of the smaller Chambers, while the seventeenth seat was alternatively from the Chamber of Middelburg-Zeeland or rotated among the five small Chambers. Amsterdam had thereby the decisive voice. The Zeelanders in particular had misgivings about this arrangement at the beginning. The fear was not unfounded, because in practice it meant Amsterdam stipulated what happened.\n</p><p>The six chambers raised the start-up capital of the Dutch East India Company:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Chamber</th>\n<th>Capital (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">Guilders</a>)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Amsterdam</td>\n<td>3,679,915\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Middelburg</td>\n<td>1,300,405\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Enkhuizen</td>\n<td>540,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Delft</td>\n<td>469,400\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Hoorn</td>\n<td>266,868\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Rotterdam</td>\n<td>173,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Total:</th>\n<th>6,424,588\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The raising of capital in Rotterdam did not go so smoothly. A considerable part originated from inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Dordrecht" title="Dordrecht">Dordrecht</a>. Although it did not raise as much capital as Amsterdam or Middelburg-Zeeland, Enkhuizen had the largest input in the <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">share</a> capital of the VOC. Under the first 358 shareholders, there were many small entrepreneurs, who dared to take the <a href="/wiki/Risk" title="Risk">risk</a>. The minimum investment in the VOC was 3,000 guilders, which priced the Company\'s stock within the means of many merchants.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg/220px-AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg/330px-AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg/440px-AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3700" data-file-height="2232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-5460-NA_Uniform_for_VOC_soldiers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Various VOC soldier uniforms, c.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1783</div></div></div>\n<p>Among the early shareholders of the VOC, immigrants played an important role. Under the 1,143 tenderers were 39 <a href="/wiki/German_people" class="mw-redirect" title="German people">Germans</a> and no fewer than 301 from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a> (roughly present Belgium and Luxembourg, then under <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> rule), of whom <a href="/wiki/Isaac_le_Maire" class="mw-redirect" title="Isaac le Maire">Isaac le Maire</a> was the largest subscriber with \xc6\x9285,000. VOC\'s total <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">capitalisation</a> was ten times that of its British rival.\n</p><p>The <i>Heeren XVII</i> (Lords Seventeen) met alternately 6 years in Amsterdam and 2 years in Middelburg-Zeeland. They defined the VOC\'s general policy and divided the tasks among the Chambers. The Chambers carried out all the necessary work, built their own ships and warehouses and traded the merchandise. The <i>Heeren XVII</i> sent the ships\' masters off with extensive instructions on the route to be navigated, prevailing winds, currents, shoals and landmarks. The VOC also produced its own <a href="/wiki/Nautical_charts" class="mw-redirect" title="Nautical charts">charts</a>.\n</p><p>In the context of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch-Portuguese_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch-Portuguese War">Dutch-Portuguese War</a> the company established its headquarters in Batavia, <a href="/wiki/Java_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Java island">Java</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>). Other colonial outposts were also established in the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, such as on the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a>, which include the <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">Banda Islands</a>, where the VOC forcibly maintained a monopoly over <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a>. Methods used to maintain the monopoly involved <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">extortion</a> and the violent suppression of the native population, including <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>  In addition, VOC representatives sometimes used the tactic of burning spice trees to force indigenous populations to grow other crops, thus artificially cutting the supply of spices like nutmeg and cloves.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_outposts">VOC outposts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: VOC outposts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Organization and leadership structures were varied as necessary in the various VOC outposts:\n</p><p><i>Opperhoofd</i> is a Dutch word (pl. <i>Opperhoofden</i>), which literally means \'supreme chief\'. In this VOC context, the word is a <a href="/wiki/Gubernatorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Gubernatorial">gubernatorial</a> title, comparable to the English <a href="/wiki/Chief_factor" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief factor">Chief factor</a>, for the chief executive officer of a Dutch <i><a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factory</a></i> in the sense of trading post, as led by a <a href="/wiki/Factor_(agent)" title="Factor (agent)">factor</a>, i.e. agent.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd><dl><dd>See more at <b><a href="/wiki/VOC_Opperhoofden_in_Japan" title="VOC Opperhoofden in Japan">VOC <i>Opperhoofden</i> in Japan</a></b></dd></dl></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_Justice_in_Batavia">Council of Justice in Batavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Council of Justice in Batavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Council of Justice in Batavia was the appellate court for all the other VOC Company posts in the VOC empire.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholder_activism_at_the_VOC_and_the_beginnings_of_modern_corporate_governance_problems">Shareholder activism at the VOC and the beginnings of modern corporate governance problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Shareholder activism at the VOC and the beginnings of modern corporate governance problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC_duit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/VOC_duit.jpg/150px-VOC_duit.jpg" width="150" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/VOC_duit.jpg/225px-VOC_duit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/VOC_duit.jpg/300px-VOC_duit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="405" data-file-height="781" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC_duit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Both sides of a <a href="/wiki/Duit" title="Duit">duit</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Coinage_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Coinage of the Dutch East India Company">coin minted in 1735 by the VOC</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The seventeenth-century Dutch businessmen, especially the VOC investors, were possibly the history\'s first recorded investors to seriously consider the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a>\'s problems.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Le_Maire" title="Isaac Le Maire">Isaac Le Maire</a>, who is known as history\'s first recorded <a href="/wiki/Short_seller" class="mw-redirect" title="Short seller">short seller</a>, was also a sizeable shareholder of the VOC. In 1609, he complained of the VOC\'s shoddy corporate governance. On 24 January 1609, Le Maire filed a petition against the VOC, marking the first recorded expression of <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_activism" class="mw-redirect" title="Shareholder activism">shareholder activism</a>. In what is the first recorded corporate governance dispute, Le Maire formally charged that the VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> (the Heeren XVII) sought to "retain another\xe2\x80\x99s money for longer or use it ways other than the latter wishes" and petitioned for the liquidation of the VOC in accordance with standard business practice.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Initially the largest single shareholder in the VOC and a <i>bewindhebber</i> sitting on the board of governors, Le Maire apparently attempted to divert the firm\'s profits to himself by undertaking 14 expeditions under his own accounts instead of those of the company. Since his large shareholdings were not accompanied by greater voting power, Le Maire was soon ousted by other governors in 1605 on charges of embezzlement, and was forced to sign an agreement not to compete with the VOC. Having retained stock in the company following this incident, in 1609 Le Maire would become the author of what is celebrated as "first recorded expression of shareholder advocacy at a publicly traded company".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1622, the history\'s first recorded <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Shareholder revolt">shareholder revolt</a> also happened among the VOC investors who complained that the company account books had been "smeared with bacon" so that they might be "eaten by dogs." The investors demanded a "reeckeninge," a proper financial audit.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The 1622 campaign by the <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a> of the VOC is a testimony of genesis of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a> (CSR) in which shareholders staged protests by distributing pamphlets and complaining about management self enrichment and secrecy.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Main_trading_posts.2C_settlements.2C_and_colonies"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_trading_posts,_settlements,_and_colonies">Main trading posts, settlements, and colonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Main trading posts, settlements, and colonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Prose" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>is in a list format that may be better presented using <a settlements</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Former_settlements_and_colonies_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" Dutch East India Company (VOC)</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> (global headquarters)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Enkhuizen" (1636\xe2\x80\x931741)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts_and_wars_involving_the_VOC">Conflicts and wars involving the VOC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Conflicts and wars involving the VOC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(July 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Military_history_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Military history of the Dutch East India Company">Military history of the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Battles_involving_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Battles involving the Dutch East India Company">Battles involving the Dutch East India Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spice_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Spice wars">Spice wars</a></div>\n<p>The history of VOC commercial conflict, for example with the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> (EIC), was at times closely connected to Dutch military conflicts.  The commercial interests of the VOC (and more generally the Netherlands) were reflected in military objectives and the settlements agreed by treaty.  In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda (1667)</a> ending the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a>, the Dutch were finally able to secure a <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg#History" title="Nutmeg">VOC monopoly for nutmeg trade</a>, ceding the island of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> to the British while gaining the last non-VOC controlled source of nutmeg, the island of Rhun in the <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands#VOC_Monopoly" title="Banda Islands">Banda islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch later re-captured <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, but returned it along with the colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Westminster_(1674)" title="Treaty of Westminster (1674)">Treaty of Westminster (1674)</a> ending the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Dutch War">Fourth Anglo-Dutch War</a>. The British also gave up claims on <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Westminster_(1674)" title="Treaty of Westminster (1674)">Treaty of Westminster</a>. There was also an effort to compensate the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company#Decline" title="Dutch West India Company">war-related losses of the Dutch West India Company</a> in the mid-17th Century by the profits of the VOC, though this was ultimately blocked.\n</p><p>Military conflicts involving the VOC (not necessarily comprehensive)\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Eighty Years\' War</a> / <a href="/wiki/Dutch_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch War of Independence">Dutch War of Independence</a> (1568\xe2\x80\x931648)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sino-Dutch_conflicts" title="Sino-Dutch conflicts">Sino-Dutch conflicts</a> (1620s\xe2\x80\x931662)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1665-1667)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1672-74)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Dutch War">Fourth Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1780-84)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Dutch_War" title="Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War">Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BB%8Bnh%E2%80%93Nguy%E1%BB%85n_War" title="Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War">Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dutch%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" title="Dutch\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War">Dutch\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Javanese_Wars_of_Succession" title="Javanese Wars of Succession">Javanese Wars of Succession</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Malayan%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayan\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War">Malayan\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sinhalese%E2%80%93Portuguese_War" title="Sinhalese\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War">Sinhalese\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese War</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi%E2%80%93Dutch_Wars" title="Khoikhoi\xe2\x80\x93Dutch Wars">Khoikhoi\xe2\x80\x93Dutch Wars</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Travancore%E2%80%93Dutch_War" title="Travancore\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War">Travancore\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_roles_and_legacy">Historical roles and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Historical roles and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">A 400-year evolution of global <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock markets</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital markets</a> in general)</div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg/200px-MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg/300px-MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg/400px-MG_056-De_Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1047" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> (or <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser" class="extiw" title="nl:Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser">Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser</a> in Dutch), the world\'s first formal <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>. The formal <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> in its modern sense \xe2\x80\x93 as one of the potent symbols of <a href="/wiki/Capitalism#Modern_capitalism" title="Capitalism">modern capitalism</a><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 was a pioneering innovation by the VOC managers and shareholders in the early 17th century.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:NYSE127.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/NYSE127.jpg/200px-NYSE127.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/NYSE127.jpg/300px-NYSE127.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/NYSE127.jpg/400px-NYSE127.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Trading_floor" class="mw-redirect" title="Trading floor">trading floor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> (NYSE) in the early 21st century \xe2\x80\x93 as one of the foremost symbols of American capitalism in the blooming era of <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg/200px-VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg" width="200" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg/300px-VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg/400px-VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1826" data-file-height="1329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VOC_aandeel_9_september_1606.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the oldest known <a href="/wiki/Stock_certificate" title="Stock certificate">stock certificates</a>, issued by the <a href="/wiki/Vereenigde_Oost-Indische_Compagnie" class="mw-redirect" title="Vereenigde Oost-Indische Compagnie">VOC</a> Chamber of <a href="/wiki/Enkhuizen" title="Enkhuizen">Enkhuizen</a>, dated 9 Sep 1606.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The VOC was the first recorded <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> to get a fixed <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital stock</a>. The VOC was also the first <a href="/wiki/Publicly_listed_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Publicly listed company">publicly listed company</a> ever to pay regular <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividends</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The VOC was possibly in fact the first ever <a href="/wiki/Blue-chip_stock" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue-chip stock">blue-chip stock</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Robert_Shiller" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Shiller">Robert Shiller</a>\'s words, the <a href="/wiki/Verenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie" class="mw-redirect" title="Verenigde Oostindische Compagnie">VOC</a> was "the first real important stock" in the history of finance.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg/220px-Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg/330px-Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg/440px-Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereenigde_Oostindische_Compagnie_spiegelretourschip_Amsterdam_replica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Founded in 1602, the Dutch East India Company (VOC), the world\'s first formally <a href="/wiki/Listing_(finance)" title="Listing (finance)">listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a>, started off as a <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trader</a>. In the same year, the VOC undertook the world\'s first recorded <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">IPO</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Go_public" class="mw-redirect" title="Go public">Going public</a>" enabled the company to raise the vast sum of 6.5 million <a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">guilders</a> quickly. The VOC\'s institutional innovations and business practices<sup id="cite_ref-Steensgaard_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steensgaard-38">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VonNordenflycht_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VonNordenflycht-40">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> laid the foundations for the rise of modern-day global corporations and <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital markets</a> that now dominate the world\'s economic systems, whether for good or bad.<sup id="cite_ref-AnupShah_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnupShah-47">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The Netherlands United East Indies Company (Verenigde Oostindische Compagnie, or VOC), founded in 1602, was the world\'s first multinational, joint-stock, limited liability corporation \xe2\x80\x93 as well as its first government-backed trading <a href="/wiki/Cartel" title="Cartel">cartel</a>. <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">Our own East India Company</a>, founded in 1600, remained a <a href="/wiki/Coffee-house" class="mw-redirect" title="Coffee-house">coffee-house</a> <a href="/wiki/Clique" title="Clique">clique</a> until 1657, when it, too, began selling shares, not in individual voyages, but in <a href="/wiki/John_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="John Company">John Company</a> itself, by which time its Dutch rival was by far the biggest commercial enterprise the world had known.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Murray_Sayle" title="Murray Sayle">Murray Sayle</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/London_Review_of_Books" title="London Review of Books">London Review of Books</a></i>, April 2001<sup id="cite_ref-MurraySayle_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MurraySayle-48">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) As populations grew, more robust legal and financial infrastructures began to develop across Europe. Those infrastructures, combined with advances in shipping technology, made large-scale trade feasible for the first time. In 1602, the Dutch East India Company was formed. It was a new type of institution: the first multinational company, and the first to issue public stock. These innovations allowed a single company to mobilize financial resources from a large number of investors and create ventures at a scale that had previously <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">only been possible for monarchs</a>.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/John_Hagel_III" title="John Hagel III">John Hagel</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/John_Seely_Brown" title="John Seely Brown">John Seely Brown</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte Insights</a></i>, March 2013<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In terms of global business history, the lessons from the VOC\'s successes or failures are critically important. In his book <i>Amsterdam: A History of the World\'s Most Liberal City</i> (2013), American author and historian <a href="/wiki/Russell_Shorto" title="Russell Shorto">Russell Shorto</a> summarizes the VOC\'s importance in world history: "Like the oceans it mastered, the VOC had a scope that is hard to fathom. One could craft a defensible argument that no company in history has had such an impact on the world. Its surviving archives\xe2\x80\x94in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, Colombo, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>\xe2\x80\x94have been measured (by a consortium applying for a UNESCO grant to preserve them) in kilometers. In innumerable ways the VOC both expanded the world and brought its far-flung regions together. It introduced Europe to Asia and Africa, and vice versa (while its sister multinational, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">West India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">set New York City in motion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">colonized Brazil</a> and the Caribbean Islands). It pioneered globalization and invented what might be the first modern bureaucracy. It advanced cartography and shipbuilding. It fostered disease, slavery, and exploitation on a scale never before imaged."<sup id="cite_ref-RussellShorto_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussellShorto-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A pioneering early model of the multinational corporation in its modern sense,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> the Company is also considered to be the world\'s first true <a href="/wiki/Transnational_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnational corporation">transnational corporation</a>. In the early 1600s, the VOC became the world\'s first formally listed <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> because it was the first corporation to be ever actually listed on a formal <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>. The VOC had a massive influence on the evolution of the modern corporation by creating an institutional prototype for subsequent large-scale <a href="/wiki/Business_enterprise" class="mw-redirect" title="Business enterprise">business enterprises</a> (in particular large corporations like multinational/transnational/global corporations) and their rise to become a highly significant socio-politico-economic force of the modern world <a href="/wiki/When_Corporations_Rule_the_World" title="When Corporations Rule the World">as we know it today</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Upbin,_Bruce_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Upbin,_Bruce-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wooldridge,_Adrian_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wooldridge,_Adrian-44">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In many respects, modern-day publicly-listed global companies (including <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Global_2000" title="Forbes Global 2000">Forbes Global 2000</a> companies)<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> are all \'descendants\' of a business model pioneered by the VOC in the 17th century. Like modern-day major corporations,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> in many ways, the post-1657 <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">English/British East India Company</a>\'s operational structure was a derivative of the earlier VOC model.<sup id="cite_ref-MurraySayle_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MurraySayle-48">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NiallFerguson2002_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NiallFerguson2002-49">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macaulay2015_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macaulay2015-32">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rajkamal2017_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajkamal2017-51">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>   \n</p><p>During its golden age, the Company played crucial roles in <a href="/wiki/Business_history" title="Business history">business</a>, financial,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;n&#93;</a></sup> socio-politico-economic, military-political, <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_history" title="Diplomatic history">diplomatic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_history" title="Ethnic history">ethnic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of Exploration">exploratory maritime</a> history of the world. In the early modern period, the VOC was also the driving force behind the rise of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">corporate-led globalization</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LowyInstitute_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LowyInstitute-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> corporate power, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate culture">corporate culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a>, corporate ethics, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_finance" title="Corporate finance">corporate finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_capitalism" title="Corporate capitalism">corporate capitalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Finance_capitalism" title="Finance capitalism">finance capitalism</a>. With its pioneering institutional innovations and powerful roles in world history,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> the Company is considered by many to be the first major, first modern,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;o&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> first global, most valuable,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and most influential corporation ever seen.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;p&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RussellShorto_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussellShorto-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taylor,_Bryan_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor,_Bryan-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The VOC was also arguably the first historical model of the <a href="/wiki/Megacorporation" title="Megacorporation">megacorporation</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutional_innovations_and_impacts_on_modern-day_global_business_practices_and_financial_system">Institutional innovations and impacts on modern-day global business practices and financial system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Institutional innovations and impacts on modern-day global business practices and financial system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic history of the Dutch Republic">Economic history of the Dutch Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Financial history of the Dutch Republic">Financial history of the Dutch Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Financial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Financial Revolution">Dutch Financial Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finance_capitalism" title="Finance capitalism">Finance capitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_finance" title="Corporate finance">Corporate finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_system" title="Financial system">Financial system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_system" title="Global financial system">Global financial system</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_financial_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="International financial centre">History of financial markets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital markets">Capital markets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_markets" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial markets">Financial markets</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_capitalism" title="History of capitalism">History of capitalism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">Corporate globalization</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange,_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg/170px-Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg" width="170" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg/255px-Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg/340px-Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange%2C_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="954" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Engraving_depicting_the_Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange,_built_by_Hendrik_de_Keyser_c._1612.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 17th-century engraving depicting the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> (Amsterdam\'s old <a href="/wiki/Exchange_(organized_market)" title="Exchange
