(organized market)">bourse</a>, a.k.a. <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser" class="extiw" title="nl:Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser">Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser</a> in Dutch), built by <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_de_Keyser" title="Hendrick de Keyser">Hendrick de Keyser</a> (c. 1612). The Amsterdam Stock Exchange (Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser), launched by the Dutch East India Company in the early 1600s, was the world\'s first official (formal) <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> when it began trading the VOC\'s freely transferable securities, including bonds and shares of stock.<sup id="cite_ref-RMurphy_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RMurphy-171">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/170px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" width="170" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/255px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg/340px-Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1051" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_de_Witte_-_De_binnenplaats_van_de_beurs_te_Amsterdam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Courtyard of the Amsterdam Stock Exchange (<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser" class="extiw" title="nl:Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser">Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser</a>) by <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_de_Witte" title="Emanuel de Witte">Emanuel de Witte</a>, 1653. The <a href="/wiki/Stock_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock trading">process of buying and selling the VOC\'s shares</a>, on the Amsterdam Stock Exchange, became the basis of the world\'s first official (formal) <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> a milestone in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_capitalism" title="History of capitalism">history of capitalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;q&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/07/EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg/170px-EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg" width="170" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/07/EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg/255px-EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/07/EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg/340px-EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="340" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EIC_Coin_1791_Half_Pice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Merchant%27s_mark" title="Merchant&#39;s mark">Merchant\'s mark</a> on <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> coin (1791). In many respects, the organizational structure and corporate practices of the VOC served as the direct model for the English/British East India Company (EIC) in the post-1657 period.<sup id="cite_ref-MurraySayle_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MurraySayle-48">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NiallFerguson2002_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NiallFerguson2002-49">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macaulay2015_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macaulay2015-32">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rajkamal2017_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rajkamal2017-51">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crowd_outside_nyse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Crowd_outside_nyse.jpg/170px-Crowd_outside_nyse.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Crowd_outside_nyse.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="251" data-file-height="349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crowd_outside_nyse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Crowd gathering on <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> (New York City) after the 1929 crash. The <a href="/wiki/1929_Wall_Street_Crash" class="mw-redirect" title="1929 Wall Street Crash">1929 Wall Street Crash</a> is often considered one of the worst <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_crash" title="Stock market crash">stock market crashes</a> in history. For good or bad,<sup id="cite_ref-Macaulay2015_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macaulay2015-32">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> the VOC-created quasi-<a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a> stock market system has profoundly influenced the evolution of the global economy since the Dutch Golden Age.</div></div></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The defining characteristics of the modern corporation, all of which emerged during the <a href="/wiki/World-systems_theory" title="World-systems theory">Dutch cycle</a>, include: <a href="/wiki/Limited_liability" title="Limited liability">limited liability</a> for investors, free transferability of investor interests, <a href="/wiki/Legal_personality" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a> and centralised management. Although some of these characteristics were present to a certain extent in the fourteenth-century <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Societas_comperarum" class="mw-redirect" title="Societas comperarum">societas comperarum</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/World-systems_theory" title="World-systems theory">first cycle</a>, the first wholly cognisable modern limited liability public company was the VOC. The organisational structures and corporate practices of the VOC were closely paralleled by the <a href="/wiki/English_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="English East India Company">English East India Company</a> and served as the direct model for all of the later mercantile trading companies of the <a href="/wiki/World-systems_theory" title="World-systems theory">second cycle</a>, including those of Italy, <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">France</a>, Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Denmark</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emden_Company" title="Emden Company">Brandenburg-Prussia</a>.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;Eric Michael Wilson, in "The Savage Republic" (2008)<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">In 1602 shares in the Dutch Vereenigde Oost-Indische Compagnie (VOC, better known as the Dutch East India Company) were issued, suddenly creating what is usually considered the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Publicly_traded_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Publicly traded company">publicly traded company</a>. (...) There are other claimants to the title of first public company, including <a href="/wiki/Bazacle_Milling_Company" title="Bazacle Milling Company">a twelfth-century water mill in France</a> and a thirteenth-century company intended to control the English wool trade, Staple of London. Its shares, however, and the manner in which those shares were traded, did not truly allow public ownership by anyone who happened to be able to afford a share. The arrival of VOC shares was therefore momentous, because as <a href="/wiki/Fernand_Braudel" title="Fernand Braudel">Fernand Braudel</a> pointed out, it opened up the ownership of companies and the ideas they generated, beyond the ranks of the aristocracy and the very rich, so that everyone could finally participate in <i>the speculative freedom of transactions</i>. By expanding ownership of its company pie for a certain price and a tentative return, the Dutch had done something historic: they had created a <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital market</a>.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;Kevin Kaiser &amp; David Young, in "The Blue Line Imperative" (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The VOC played a crucial role in the rise of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">corporate-led globalization</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_finance" title="Corporate finance">corporate finance</a>, modern <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Financial_capitalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial capitalism">financial capitalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taylor,_Bryan_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor,_Bryan-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> During its golden age, the Company made some fundamental institutional innovations in <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Netherlands_(1500%E2%80%931815)" title="Economic history of the Netherlands (1500\xe2\x80\x931815)">economic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Financial history of the Dutch Republic">financial history</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre#Amsterdam_and_the_financial_revolution_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Financial centre">financially revolutionary innovations</a> allowed a single <a href="/wiki/Company" title="Company">company</a> (like the VOC) to mobilize financial resources from a large number of investors and create ventures at a scale that had previously only been possible for monarchs. In the words of Canadian historian and sinologist <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Brook" title="Timothy Brook">Timothy Brook</a>, "the Dutch East India Company \xe2\x80\x94 the VOC, as it is known \xe2\x80\x94 is to <a href="/wiki/Corporate_capitalism" title="Corporate capitalism">corporate capitalism</a> what <a href="/wiki/Kite_experiment" title="Kite experiment">Benjamin Franklin\'s kite</a> is to <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>: the beginning of something momentous that could not have been predicted at the time."<sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The birth and growth of the VOC (especially in the 17th century) is considered by many to be the official beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">corporate globalization</a> era with the rise of large-scale <a href="/wiki/Business_enterprise" class="mw-redirect" title="Business enterprise">business enterprises</a> (multinational/transnational corporations in particular) as a highly formidable socio-politico-economic force<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> that significantly affects people\'s lives in every corner of the world today,<sup id="cite_ref-Upbin,_Bruce_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Upbin,_Bruce-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harlan_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlan-43">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LaFrance_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaFrance-45">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wooldridge,_Adrian_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wooldridge,_Adrian-44">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zahra_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahra-46">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> whether for better or worse.<sup id="cite_ref-AnupShah_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AnupShah-47">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> As the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Publicly_traded_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Publicly traded company">publicly traded company</a> and first <a href="/wiki/Listed_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Listed company">listed company</a> (the first company to be ever <a href="/wiki/Listing_(finance)" title="Listing (finance)">listed</a> on an official stock exchange), the VOC was the first company to issue <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> to the general public. Considered by many experts to be the world\'s first truly (modern) <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> the VOC was also the first permanently organized <a href="/wiki/Limited_liability_company" title="Limited liability company">limited-liability</a> <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a>, with a permanent <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital</a> base.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;r&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The VOC shareholders were the pioneers in laying the basis for modern <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corporate_finance" title="Corporate finance">corporate finance</a>. The VOC is often considered as the precursor of modern corporations, if not the first truly modern corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> It was the VOC that invented the idea of investing in the company rather than in a specific venture governed by the company. With its pioneering features such as <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a> (first globally recognized <a href="/wiki/Corporate_logo" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate logo">corporate logo</a>), entrepreneurial spirit, <a href="/wiki/Legal_personality" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal personality">legal personhood</a>, transnational (multinational) operational structure, high and stable profitability, permanent <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital</a> (fixed capital stock),<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> freely transferable <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Securities_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities trading">tradable securities</a>, separation of <a href="/wiki/Ownership" title="Ownership">ownership</a> and <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Limited_liability" title="Limited liability">limited liability</a> for both <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a> and managers, the VOC is generally considered a major institutional breakthrough<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and the model for large <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporations</a> that now dominate the <a href="/wiki/Global_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Global economy">global economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Dam_in_Amsterdam,_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg/170px-The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg" width="170" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg/255px-The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg/340px-The_Dam_in_Amsterdam%2C_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3775" data-file-height="2372" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Dam_in_Amsterdam,_by_Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Dam_Square" title="Dam Square">Dam Square</a> in Amsterdam, by <a href="/wiki/Gerrit_Adriaensz_Berckheyde" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerrit Adriaensz Berckheyde">Gerrit Adriaensz Berckheyde</a>, c. 1660. In the picture of the centre of highly cosmopolitan and tolerant Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>/<a href="/wiki/Oriental" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental">Oriental</a> figures (possibly <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> or <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a> merchants) are shown negotiating. While the VOC was a major force behind the <a href="/wiki/Economic_miracle" title="Economic miracle">economic miracle</a> of the Dutch Republic in the 17th-century, the VOC\'s institutional innovations played a decisive role in the rise of Amsterdam as the first modern model of a (global) <a href="/wiki/International_financial_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="International financial centre">international financial centre</a>.</div></div></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">The <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> \xe2\x80\x94 the daytime adventure serial of the well-to-do \xe2\x80\x94 would not be the stock market if it did not have its ups and downs. (...) Apart from the economic advantages and disadvantages of stock exchanges \xe2\x80\x94 the advantage that they provide a free flow of capital to finance industrial expansion, for instance, and the disadvantage that they provide an all too convenient way for the unlucky, the imprudent, and the gullible to lose their money \xe2\x80\x94 their development has created a whole pattern of social behavior, complete with customs, language, and predictable responses to given events. What is truly extraordinary is the speed with which this pattern emerged full blown following the establishment, in 1611, of the world\'s first important stock exchange \xe2\x80\x94 <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser" class="extiw" title="nl:Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser">a roofless courtyard in Amsterdam</a> \xe2\x80\x94 and the degree to which it persists (with variations, it is true) on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> in the nineteen-sixties. Present-day <a href="/wiki/Stock_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock trading">stock trading</a> in the United States \xe2\x80\x94 a bewilderingly vast enterprise, involving millions of miles of private telegraph wires, computers that can read and copy the Manhattan Telephone Directory in three minutes, and over twenty million <a href="/wiki/Stockholder" class="mw-redirect" title="Stockholder">stockholder</a> participants \xe2\x80\x94 would seem to be a far cry from a handful of seventeenth-century Dutchmen haggling in the rain. But the field marks are much the same. The first stock exchange was, inadvertently, a laboratory in which new human reactions were revealed. By the same token, the New York Stock Exchange is also a sociological test tube, forever contributing to the human species\' self-understanding. The behaviour of the pioneering Dutch <a href="/wiki/Stock_trader" title="Stock trader">stock traders</a> is ably documented in a book entitled "Confusion of Confusions," written by a plunger on the Amsterdam market named <a href="/wiki/Joseph_de_la_Vega" title="Joseph de la Vega">Joseph de la Vega</a>; originally published in 1688 (...)\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/John_Brooks_(writer)" title="John Brooks (writer)">John Brooks</a>, in "Business Adventures" (1968)<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Business ventures with multiple shareholders became popular with <i>commenda</i> contracts in <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">medieval Italy</a> (Greif 2006, 286), and Malmendier (2009) provides evidence that shareholder companies date back to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">ancient Rome</a>. Yet the title of the world\'s first stock market deservedly goes to that of seventeenth-century Amsterdam, where an active <a href="/wiki/Secondary_market" title="Secondary market">secondary market</a> in <a href="/wiki/Company_shares" class="mw-redirect" title="Company shares">company shares</a> emerged. The two major companies were the Dutch East India Company and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a>, founded in 1602 and 1621. Other companies existed, but they were not as large and constituted a small portion of the stock market (Israel [1989] 1991, 109\xe2\x80\x93112; Dehing and \'t Hart 1997, 54; de la Vega [1688] 1996, 173).\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Edward_P._Stringham" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward P. Stringham">Edward P. Stringham</a> &amp; Nicholas A. Curott, in "The Oxford Handbook of Austrian Economics" [<i>On the Origins of Stock Markets</i>] (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The VOC was a driving force behind the rise of Amsterdam as the first modern model of <a href="/wiki/International_financial_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="International financial centre">international financial centres</a><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;s&#93;</a></sup> that now dominate the <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_system" title="Global financial system">global financial system</a>. With its maritime and financial power, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Republican-period</a> Amsterdam \xe2\x80\x93 unlike its <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlandish</a> cousins and predecessors such as <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Netherlands" title="Burgundian Netherlands">Burgundian-period</a> <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Netherlands" title="Habsburg Netherlands">Habsburg-period</a> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 could control crucial resources and markets directly, sending its fleets to almost all quarters of the globe. During the 17th century and most of the 18th century, Amsterdam had been the most influential financial centre of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The VOC also played a major role in the creation of the world\'s first fully functioning <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial market</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> with the birth of a fully fledged <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch were also the first who effectively used a fully-fledged capital market (including the <a href="/wiki/Bond_market" title="Bond market">bond market</a> and the stock market) to finance companies (such as the VOC and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">WIC</a>). It was in the 17th-century Dutch Republic that the global <a href="/wiki/Securities_market" title="Securities market">securities market</a> began to take on its modern form. And it was in Amsterdam that the important institutional innovations such as publicly traded companies, transnational corporations, capital markets (including bond markets and stock markets), <a href="/wiki/Central_banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Central banking">central banking</a> system, <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment banking</a> system, and <a href="/wiki/Investment_fund" title="Investment fund">investment funds</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mutual_fund" title="Mutual fund">mutual funds</a>) were systematically operated for the first time in history. In 1602 the VOC established an <a href="/wiki/Exchange_(organized_market)" title="Exchange (organized market)">exchange</a> in Amsterdam where VOC stock and bonds could be traded in a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_market" title="Secondary market">secondary market</a>. The VOC undertook the world\'s first recorded <a href="/wiki/IPO" class="mw-redirect" title="IPO">IPO</a> in the same year. The Amsterdam Stock Exchange (<i>Amsterdamsche Beurs</i> or <i>Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser</i> in Dutch) was also the world\'s first fully-fledged stock exchange. While the <a href="/wiki/Italian_city-states" title="Italian city-states">Italian city-states</a> produced first formal <a href="/wiki/Bond_market" title="Bond market">bond markets</a>, they didn\'t develop the other ingredient necessary to produce a fully fledged capital market: the formal stock market.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch East India Company (VOC) became the first company to offer <a href="/wiki/Share_(finance)" title="Share (finance)">shares</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a>. The dividend averaged around 18% of capital over the course of the Company\'s 200-year existence. The launch of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a> by the VOC in the early 1600s, has long been recognized as the origin of \'modern\' stock exchanges that specialize in creating and sustaining <a href="/wiki/Secondary_market" title="Secondary market">secondary markets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">securities</a> (such as bonds and shares of stock) issued by corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Dutch investors were the first to trade their shares at a regular stock exchange. The <a href="/wiki/Stock_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock trading">process of buying and selling these shares of stock</a> in the VOC became the basis of the first official (formal) <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> in history.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RMurphy_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RMurphy-171">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> It was in the Dutch Republic that the early techniques of <a href="/wiki/Market_manipulation" title="Market manipulation">stock-market manipulation</a> were developed. The Dutch pioneered <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">stock futures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stock_options" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock options">stock options</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short_selling" class="mw-redirect" title="Short selling">short selling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bear_raid" title="Bear raid">bear raids</a>, debt-equity swaps, and other <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculative instruments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stringham_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stringham-215">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Amsterdam businessman <a href="/wiki/Joseph_de_la_Vega" title="Joseph de la Vega">Joseph de la Vega</a>\'s <i>Confusion of Confusions</i> (1688)<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> was the earliest book about <a href="/wiki/Stock_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock trading">stock trading</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Impacts_on_social.2C_economic.2C_financial.2C_political.2C_and_military_history_of_the_Netherlands"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Impacts_on_social,_economic,_financial,_political,_and_military_history_of_the_Netherlands">Impacts on social, economic, financial, political, and military history of the Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Impacts on social, economic, financial, political, and military history of the Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Netherlands_(1500%E2%80%931815)" title="Economic history of the Netherlands (1500\xe2\x80\x931815)">Economic history of the Netherlands (1500\xe2\x80\x931815)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic history of the Dutch Republic">Dutch economic miracle (c. 1590s\xe2\x80\x931600s)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Financial_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Financial Revolution">Dutch Financial Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Voc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Voc.jpg/170px-Voc.jpg" width="170" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Voc.jpg/255px-Voc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Voc.jpg/340px-Voc.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1356" data-file-height="1074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Voc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">shipyard</a> of the United East India Company (VOC) in Amsterdam (1726 engraving by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mulder" title="Joseph Mulder">Joseph Mulder</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Zaan" title="Zaan">Zaan</a>, near Amsterdam, became one of the world\'s earliest known <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialized</a> areas, with around 900 wind-powered <a href="/wiki/Sawmills" class="mw-redirect" title="Sawmills">sawmills</a> at the end of the 17th century. By the early seventeenth century Dutch shipyards were producing a large number of ships to a standard design, allowing extensive <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labour" title="Division of labour">division of labour</a>, a specialization which further reduced <a href="/wiki/Unit_cost" title="Unit cost">unit costs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) I don\'t understand why you\'re all being so negative and unpleasant. Let\'s just be happy with each other. Let\'s just say \xe2\x80\x9cthe Netherlands can do it\xe2\x80\x9d again: that VOC mentality. Look across our borders. Dynamism! Don\'t you think?\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieter_Balkenende" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Pieter Balkenende">Jan Pieter Balkenende</a>, then Dutch Prime Minister, reacted to the criticism of his government policy during the parliamentary debate, September 2006<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;t&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) The charter of the Dutch East India Company stipulated that any Dutch citizen could buy shares in the company. Many did grasp this opportunity. And they were not only wealthy merchants! Among these first shareholders were corn dealers, grocers, bakers, brewers, tailors, seamstresses, sail makers, carpenters, cobblers and servants. One of the most modest participants was the Mayor of Amsterdam\'s <a href="/wiki/Maid" title="Maid">maid</a>. Her name was Grietje Dirksdochter. Grietje saw a tipping point in Dutch history. This new opening provided ordinary people like her not only with the opportunity of becoming a shareholder of a mere shipping company. It provided her with the opportunity of becoming a shareholder of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>. Of an exciting era of social development and economic growth. She was taking part in a new, dynamic economy.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Queen_M%C3%A1xima_of_the_Netherlands" title="Queen M\xc3\xa1xima of the Netherlands">Queen M\xc3\xa1xima of the Netherlands</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Investment_banker" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment banker">investment banker</a>, speech at fourth annual Morningstar Investment Conference in Amsterdam, March 2014<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The idea of a highly competitive and organized (active mainly in <a href="/wiki/Greater_India" title="Greater India">Greater India</a> but <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">headquartered</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces of the Netherlands">United Provinces of the Netherlands</a>) Dutch government-backed privately-financed military-commercial enterprise was the wartime brainchild of the leading republican statesman <a href="/wiki/Johan_van_Oldenbarnevelt" title="Johan van Oldenbarnevelt">Johan van Oldenbarnevelt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Dutch Republic">States-General</a> in the late 1590s. In 1602, the "United" East India Company (VOC) was formed by a <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Dutch Republic">government-directed</a> <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_(business)" title="Consolidation (business)">consolidation/amalgamation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">several rival Dutch trading companies</a> or the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> It was a time when the newly formed Dutch Republic was in the midst of their <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">eighty-year-long revolutionary global war</a> against the mighty <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> (1579\xe2\x80\x931648).<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> And therefore, from the beginning, the VOC was not only a business enterprise but also an instrument of war. In other words, the VOC was a fully functioning military-political-commercial complex in its own right rather than a pure trading company or shipping company.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;u&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) Only a unique federal state such as the Dutch Republic could have dreamed up a federal company structure. The VOC combined flexibility with strength, giving the Dutch a huge advantage in the competition to dominate maritime trade to Asia. Within a few decades, the VOC proved itself to be the most powerful trading corporation in the seventeenth-century world and the model for the large-scale business enterprises that now dominate the global economy.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Timothy_Brook" title="Timothy Brook">Timothy Brook</a>, in "<a href="/wiki/Vermeer%27s_Hat" title="Vermeer&#39;s Hat">Vermeer\'s Hat</a>" (2008)<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the early modern period, the VOC was the largest private <a href="/wiki/Employer" class="mw-redirect" title="Employer">employer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a>. The Company was a major force behind the <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre#Amsterdam_and_the_financial_revolution_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Financial centre">financial revolution</a><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;v&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_miracle" title="Economic miracle">economic miracle</a><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> of the young Dutch Republic in the 17th century. During their <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Golden Age</a>, the Dutch Republic (or the Northern Netherlands), as the resource-poor and obscure cousins of the more urbanized <a href="/wiki/Southern_Netherlands" title="Southern Netherlands">Southern Netherlands</a>, rose to become the world\'s leading economic and financial superpower.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;w&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Despite its lack of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a> (except for water and <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>) and its comparatively modest size and population, the Dutch Republic dominated global market in many advanced industries<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> such as shipbuilding, shipping, water engineering, printing and publishing, map making, <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry" title="Pulp and paper industry">pulp and paper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lens_(optics)" title="Lens (optics)">lens-making</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_refinery" title="Sugar refinery">sugarcane refining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overseas_investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas investment">overseas investment</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">international trade</a>. The Dutch Republic was an early <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialized</a> nation-state in its Golden Age. The 17th-century Dutch mechanical innovations/inventions such as <a href="/wiki/Wind-powered" class="mw-redirect" title="Wind-powered">wind-powered</a> <a href="/wiki/Sawmill" title="Sawmill">sawmills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hollander_beater" title="Hollander beater">Hollander beaters</a> helped revolutionize shipbuilding and <a href="/wiki/Pulp_and_paper_industry" title="Pulp and paper industry">paper (including pulp)</a><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;x&#93;</a></sup> industries in the early modern period. The VOC\'s shipyards also contributed greatly to the Dutch domination of global <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shipping_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping industry">shipping</a> industries during the 1600s.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;y&#93;</a></sup> "By seventeenth century standards," as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Unger" title="Richard Unger">Richard Unger</a> affirms, Dutch shipbuilding "was a massive industry and larger than any shipbuilding industry which had preceded it."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> By the 1670s the size of the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Merchant_fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant fleet">merchant fleet</a> probably exceeded the combined fleets of England, France, Spain, Portugal, and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Until the mid-1700s, the <a href="/wiki/Category:Economic_history_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Category:Economic history of the Dutch Republic">economic system of the Dutch Republic</a> (including its financial system) was the most advanced and sophisticated ever seen in history.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> From about 1600 to 1720, the Dutch had the highest <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> in the world, at least double that of neighbouring countries at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>However, in a typical <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism_in_the_Netherlands" title="Multiculturalism in the Netherlands">multicultural society of the Netherlands</a> (home to one million citizens with roots in the former colonies Indonesia, Suriname and the Antilles),<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> the VOC\'s history (and especially its dark side) has always been a potential source of controversy. In 2006 when the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Prime Minister">Dutch Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieter_Balkenende" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Pieter Balkenende">Jan Pieter Balkenende</a> referred to the pioneering entrepreneurial spirit and <a href="/wiki/Work_ethic" title="Work ethic">work ethics</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">their Golden Age</a>, he coined the term "VOC mentality" (<i><a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/VOC-mentaliteit" class="extiw" title="nl:VOC-mentaliteit">VOC-mentaliteit</a></i> in Dutch).<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;z&#93;</a></sup> For Balkenende, the VOC represented Dutch <a href="/wiki/Business_acumen" title="Business acumen">business acumen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a>, adventurous spirit, and decisiveness. However, it unleashed a wave of criticism, since such romantic views about the Dutch Golden Age ignores the inherent historical associations with colonialism, exploitation and violence. Balkenende later stressed that "it had not been his intention to refer to that at all".<sup id="cite_ref-voc_mentality_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voc_mentality-264">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> But in spite of criticisms, the "VOC-mentality", as a characteristic of the selective historical perspective on the Dutch Golden Age, has been considered a key feature of Dutch cultural policy for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-voc_mentality_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voc_mentality-264">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roles_in_the_history_of_the_global_economy_and_international_relations">Roles in the history of the global economy and international relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Roles in the history of the global economy and international relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg/220px-4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg/330px-4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg/440px-4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3228" data-file-height="2153" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:4_color_mix_of_peppercorns.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper#Green_pepper" title="Black pepper">green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_pepper" class="mw-redirect" title="Pink pepper">pink</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_pepper" class="mw-redirect" title="White pepper">white peppercorns</a>. In terms of <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a>, the VOC was an early pioneering model of the <a href="/wiki/Global_supply_chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Global supply chain">global supply chain</a> in its modern sense.<sup id="cite_ref-LowyInstitute_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LowyInstitute-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Dutch word \xe2\x80\x9cpeperduur\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 which literally translated as \xe2\x80\x9cpepper expensive\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9cas expensive as pepper\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 is an expression for something that is very costly.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Foreign_relations_of_the_Dutch_Republic" title="Category:Foreign relations of the Dutch Republic">Foreign relations of the Dutch Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate globalization">Corporate globalization (economic globalization)</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">International trade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_history_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Political history of South Africa">Political history of South Africa</a>, <a title="Freedom of the seas">Freedom of the seas</a></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Its [the VOC\'s] fame as the first <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a>, which heralded the transition from feudalism to modern capitalism,<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;aa&#93;</a></sup> and its remarkable financial success for nearly two centuries ensure its importance in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_capitalism" title="History of capitalism">history of capitalism</a>.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;Warwick Funnell &amp; Jeffrey Robertson, in "Accounting by the First Public Company" (2014)<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) Here [17th-century <a href="/wiki/Ternate_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Ternate Island">Ternate</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Maluku" title="North Maluku">North Maluku</a>, Indonesia], surely, was a very early, fully operational manifestation of international integration, the embryonic form of today\'s ubiquitous globalisation. We would recognise its constituent elements. Here was the tenuous but well-structured <a href="/wiki/Supply-chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Supply-chain">supply-chain</a>, extended all the way from <a href="/wiki/Banda_Islands" title="Banda Islands">Banda</a> to Amsterdam, via numerous ports and functionaries, administered with brutal efficiency by the Dutch East India Company, perhaps the first business organisation that bears resemblance to today\'s multinational corporations. The company raised money by issuing shares. It had the first widely-recognised commercial logo. Even without today\'s computers, the company\'s officials were linked through a hierarchy of regular detailed reporting and accounting. Production was brought together in plantations and processed in \'factories\'. Near-subsistence agriculture was replaced with scale and quality control, supervised by the <i>perkeniers</i> with an incentivising profit-sharing deal with the company. Customer feedback was insistently relayed to producers: \'small nutmegs are of no value\'. This mighty machine produced 3000 tons of <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> annually and transported it across hazardous waters to deliver it to the burghers of Holland and on to the rest of Europe\'s spice-hungry upper-class. Ad hoc trade between nations, with goods passing through many hands, many owners and many markets, was replaced by \'straight-through\' processing by a single entity \xe2\x80\x93 the Dutch East India Company.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; id="cite_ref-LowyInstitute_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LowyInstitute-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" href="/wiki/File:The_arrival_of_King_Charles_II_of_England_in_Rotterdam,_may_24_1660_(Lieve_Pietersz._Verschuier,_1665).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The arrival of King Charles II of England in Rotterdam, 24 May 1660</i> by <a href="/wiki/Lieve_Verschuier" title="Lieve Verschuier">Lieve Verschuier</a>. <a href="/wiki/King_Charles_II_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="King Charles II of England">King Charles II of England</a> sailed from <a href="/wiki/Breda" title="Breda">Breda</a> to <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a> in May 1660 in a <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yacht</a> owned by the VOC. <i><a href="/wiki/HMY_Mary" title="HMY Mary">HMY Mary</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/HMY_Bezan" title="HMY Bezan">HMY Bezan</a></i> (both were built by the VOC) were given to Charles II, on the restoration of the monarchy, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Gift" title="Dutch Gift">Dutch Gift</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg/170px-Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg" width="170" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg/255px-Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg/340px-Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1875" data-file-height="1198" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas_Blaeu-Van_der_Hem_-_Taioan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overview of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Zeelandia_(Taiwan)" title="Fort Zeelandia (Taiwan)">Fort Zeelandia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Dutch Formosa</a> (in the 17th-century). It was in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">the Dutch rule period of Taiwan</a> that the VOC began to encourage large-scale <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Chinese" title="Mainland Chinese">mainland Chinese</a> immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> As an early modern pioneer of outward <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> (FDI),<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moore,_Jason_W._p._188_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moore,_Jason_W._p._188-270">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> the VOC\'s economic activities changed the <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history" title="Demographic history">demographic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Taiwan" title="Economic history of Taiwan">economic history of the island</a> forever.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg/170px-S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg" width="170" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg/255px-S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg/340px-S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1144" data-file-height="856" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%BCdafrika_Franschhoek_Weingut2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">Vineyard</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Paarl" title="Paarl">Paarl</a> ward of <a href="/wiki/Franschhoek" title="Franschhoek">Franschhoek</a> (<a href="/wiki/Western_Cape_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Cape Province">Western Cape Province</a>). The <a href="/wiki/South_African_wine" title="South African wine">South African wine industry</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_World_wine" title="New World wine">New World wine</a>) is among the lasting legacy of the VOC era.</div></div></div>\n<p>The VOC was a transcontinental <a href="/wiki/Employer" class="mw-redirect" title="Employer">employer</a> and an early pioneer of outward <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> at the dawn of modern capitalism. In his book <i>The Ecology of Money: Debt, Growth, and Sustainability</i> (2013), Adrian Kuzminski notes, "The Dutch, it seems, more than anyone in the West since the palmy days of ancient Rome, had more money than they knew what to do with. They discovered, unlike the Romans, that the best use of money was to make more money. They invested it, mostly in overseas ventures, utilizing the innovation of the joint-stock company in which private investors could purchase shares, the most famous being the Dutch East India Company."<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> The VOC\'s intercontinental activities played a major role to the Dutch Republic\'s prosperity, as well as it could awaken socio-economic dynamism elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moore,_Jason_W._p._188_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moore,_Jason_W._p._188-270">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Wherever Dutch capital went, urban features were developed, economic activities expanded, new industries established, new jobs created, trading companies operated, swamps drained, mines opened, forests exploited, canals constructed, mills turned, and ships were built. In the early modern period, the Dutch were pioneering capitalists who raised the commercial and industrial potential of underdeveloped or undeveloped lands whose resources they exploited, whether for better or worse. For example, the native economies of pre-VOC era Taiwan<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;ab&#93;</a></sup> and South Africa were virtually undeveloped or were in almost primitive states. In many way, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Taiwan" title="Economic history of Taiwan">recorded economic history of Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_South_Africa" title="Economic history of South Africa">South Africa</a> began with the golden age of the VOC in the 17th century. It was VOC people who established and developed the first <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> in the history of Taiwan (<a href="/wiki/Tainan" title="Tainan">Tainan</a>) and South Africa (including <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stellenbosch" title="Stellenbosch">Stellenbosch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swellendam" title="Swellendam">Swellendam</a>).\n</p><p>The VOC existed for almost 200 years from its founding in 1602, when the <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Netherlands">States-General of the Netherlands</a> granted it a 21-year monopoly over Dutch operations in Asia until its demise in 1796. During those two centuries (between 1602 and 1796), the VOC sent almost a million Europeans to work in the Asia trade on 4,785 ships, and netted for their efforts more than 2.5 million tons of Asian trade goods. By contrast, the rest of Europe combined sent only 882,412 people from 1500 to 1795, and the fleet of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> (later <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_British_Empire" title="Territorial evolution of the British Empire">British</a>) <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>, the VOC\'s nearest competitor, was a distant second to its total traffic with 2,690 ships and a mere one-fifth the tonnage of goods carried by the VOC. The VOC enjoyed huge profits from its spice monopoly through most of the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> By 1669, the VOC was the richest company the world had ever seen, with over 150 merchant ships, 40 warships, 50,000 employees, a private army of 10,000 soldiers, and a <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividend</a> payment of 40% on the original investment.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">A CorporNation\'s vast global influence<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> enables it to function simultaneously in two realms: a <a href="/wiki/For-profit_company" class="mw-redirect" title="For-profit company">for-profit company</a>, and as a force that can shape the <a href="/wiki/Geopolitical" class="mw-redirect" title="Geopolitical">geopolitical</a> landscape. <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> isn\'t the only CorporNation; <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> is clearly in that category \xe2\x80\x94 as the <a href="/wiki/Greek_debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek debt crisis">Greek political crisis</a> has revealed, the company has been a partner in deceit with governments that used financial alchemy to disguise deficits as off-balance sheet baubles. <a href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> functioned as a CorporNation during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a>. CorporNations aren\'t new. Indeed, they are as old as capitalism, going back to the Dutch East India Company, which was chartered in 1602, became the world\'s first global company and transformed Holland into a colonial power as it dominated the East.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Adam_Hanft" title="Adam Hanft">Adam Hanft</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Huffington Post">Huffington Post</a></i>, May 2010<sup id="cite_ref-AdamHanft_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdamHanft-56">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In terms of military-political history, the VOC, along with the Dutch West India Company (WIC/GWIC), was seen as the international arm of the Dutch Republic and the symbolic power of the Dutch Empire. The VOC was historically a military-political-economic complex rather than a pure <a href="/wiki/Trading_company" title="Trading company">trading company</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Shipping_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping company">shipping company</a>). The government-backed but privately financed company was effectively a state in its own right, or a <a href="/wiki/State_within_a_state" title="State within a state">state within another state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;ac&#93;</a></sup> For almost 200 years of its existence, the VOC was a key non-state geopolitical player in Eurasia.<sup id="cite_ref-AtsushiOta_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtsushiOta-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The Company was much an unofficial representative of the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General of the United Provinces</a> in foreign relations of the Dutch Republic with many states, especially Dutch-Asian relations. The Company\'s territories were even larger than some countries.\n</p><p>The VOC had seminal influences on the modern history of many countries and territories around the world such as <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> (<a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_(state)" title="History of New York (state)">New York</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malacca" title="Dutch Malacca">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_India" title="Dutch India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa" title="History of South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Taiwan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Artistic.2C_scientific.2C_technological.2C_and_cultural_legacies_of_the_VOC_World"></span><span class="mw-headline" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) Much has also been learned about the VOC and Dutch colonial societies. Moreover, the TANAP (Towards a New Age of Partnership, 2000\xe2\x80\x932007) project has created momentum for research on the relationship between the VOC and indigenous societies. In contrast, the role of the VOC in <a href="/wiki/Cultural_history" title="Cultural history">cultural history</a> and especially in the history of <a href="/wiki/Visual_culture" title="Visual culture">visual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Material_culture" title="Material culture">material culture</a> has not yet attracted comparable interest. To be sure, journals and other travel accounts (some even with illustrations) by soldiers, shippers, and VOC officials among others have been utilized as sources.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px;
