id="VOC_World_as_an_information.2Fknowledge_exchange_network_in_the_Dutch_maritime_world-system"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_World_as_an_information/knowledge_exchange_network_in_the_Dutch_maritime_world-system">VOC World as an information/knowledge exchange network in the Dutch maritime world-system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: VOC World as an information/knowledge exchange network in the Dutch maritime world-system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">Rangaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Hamel" title="Hendrick Hamel">Hendrick Hamel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hansken" title="Hansken">Hansken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_swan" title="Black swan">Black swan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">Dodo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HortusMalabaricus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/HortusMalabaricus.jpg/170px-HortusMalabaricus.jpg" width="170" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/HortusMalabaricus.jpg/255px-HortusMalabaricus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/HortusMalabaricus.jpg/340px-HortusMalabaricus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="627" data-file-height="999" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HortusMalabaricus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cover of the <i><a href="/wiki/Hortus_Malabaricus" title="Hortus Malabaricus">Hortus Malabaricus</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_van_Rheede" title="Hendrik van Rheede">Hendrik Adriaan van Reede tot Drakenstein</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9,_1707-1778,_botanist,_professor_(Alexander_Roslin)_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-170px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-255px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif/lossy-page1-340px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9%2C_1707-1778%2C_botanist%2C_professor_%28Alexander_Roslin%29_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3032" data-file-height="3655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9,_1707-1778,_botanist,_professor_(Alexander_Roslin)_-_Nationalmuseum_-_15723.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Carl Linnaeus</a> (Carl von Linn\xc3\xa9) <a href="/wiki/George_Clifford_III" title="George Clifford III">lived and studied for three years, from 1735 until 1738, in the Dutch Republic</a> \xe2\x80\x94 a seminal period in his life and career. VOC people\'s scientific contributions had a considerable influence on his work.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> VOC physician <a href="/wiki/Carl_Peter_Thunberg" title="Carl Peter Thunberg">Carl Peter Thunberg</a> (1743\xe2\x80\x931828) was one of the <a href="/wiki/Apostles_of_Linnaeus" title="Apostles of Linnaeus">Apostles of Linnaeus</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Swan_River,Perth,Western_Australia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg/170px-Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg" width="170" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg/255px-Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg/340px-Swan_River%2CPerth%2CWestern_Australia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="858" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Swan_River,Perth,Western_Australia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Black_swan" title="Black swan">Black swans</a> on the shore of the <a href="/wiki/Swan_River_(Western_Australia)" title="Swan River (Western Australia)">Swan River (Western Australia)</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> skyline in the background. The thousand-year-old conclusion "all swans are white" was disproved by the VOC navigator <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Vlamingh" title="Willem de Vlamingh">Willem de Vlamingh</a>\'s 1697 discovery.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a>, the Dutch \xe2\x80\x93 using their expertise in doing business, cartography, shipbuilding, seafaring and navigation \xe2\x80\x93 traveled to the far corners of the world, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_linguistic_influence_on_naval_terms" title="Dutch linguistic influence on naval terms">leaving their language</a> embedded in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_place_names_of_Dutch_origin" title="List of place names of Dutch origin">names of many places</a>. Dutch exploratory voyages revealed largely unknown <a href="/wiki/Landmass" class="mw-redirect" title="Landmass">landmasses</a> to the civilized world and put their names on the <a href="/wiki/World_map" title="World map">world map</a>. During the Golden Age of Dutch exploration (c. 1590s\xe2\x80\x931720s) and the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Netherlandish_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography">Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography</a> (c. 1570s\xe2\x80\x931670s), <a href="/wiki/Greater_Netherlands" title="Greater Netherlands">Dutch-speaking</a> navigators, explorers, and cartographers were the undisputed firsts to chart/map many hitherto largely unknown regions of the earth <a href="/wiki/History_of_cartography#Dutch_celestial_cartography_in_the_Age_of_Exploration" title="History of cartography">and the sky</a>. <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Dutch_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Dutch cartography">The Dutch came to dominate the map-making and map printing industry</a> by virtue of their own travels, trade ventures, and widespread commercial networks.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> As Dutch ships reached into the unknown corners of the globe, Dutch cartographers incorporated new geographical discoveries into their work. Instead of using the information themselves secretly, they published it, so the maps multiplied freely. For almost 200 years, the Dutch dominated <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">world trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> Dutch ships carried goods, but they also opened up opportunities for the exchange of knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> The commercial networks of the Dutch transnational companies, i.e. the VOC and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">West India Company</a> (WIC/GWIC), provided an infrastructure which was accessible to people with a scholarly interest in the exotic world.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Bookkeeper" class="mw-redirect" title="Bookkeeper">bookkeeper</a> <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Hamel" title="Hendrick Hamel">Hendrick Hamel</a> was the first known European/Westerner to experience first-hand and write about <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;ad&#93;</a></sup> In his report (published in the Dutch Republic) in 1666 Hendrick Hamel described his adventures on the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> and gave the first accurate description of daily life of <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">Koreans</a> to the western world.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The VOC trade post on <a href="/wiki/Dejima" title="Dejima">Dejima</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_island" title="Artificial island">artificial island</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>, was for more than two hundred years the only place where Europeans were permitted to trade with Japan. <a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">Rangaku</a> (literally \'Dutch Learning\', and by extension \'Western Learning\') is a body of knowledge developed by <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> through its contacts with the Dutch enclave of <a href="/wiki/Dejima" title="Dejima">Dejima</a>, which allowed <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> to keep abreast of <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> in the period when the country was closed to foreigners, 1641\xe2\x80\x931853, because of the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>\'s policy of national isolation (<a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">sakoku</a>).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences_on_Dutch_Golden_Age_art">Influences on Dutch Golden Age art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Influences on Dutch Golden Age art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Art_of_the_Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Category:Art of the Dutch Golden Age">Art of the Dutch Golden Age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">Dutch Golden Age painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delftware" title="Delftware">Delftware (Delft Blue)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_porcelain_in_European_painting" title="Chinese porcelain in European painting">Chinese porcelain in European painting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Exoticism" title="Exoticism">Exoticism</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg/170px-Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg" width="170" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg/255px-Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg/340px-Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="343" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hansken.rembrandt.1637.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hansken" title="Hansken">Hansken</a>, a young female <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a> from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Dutch Ceylon</a>, was brought to Amsterdam in 1637, aboard a VOC ship. <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>\'s Hansken drawing is believed to be an early portrait of one of the first Asian elephants described by science.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg/170px-Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg" width="170" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg/255px-Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg/340px-Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandtselfportraitweb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Self-portraits_by_Rembrandt" title="Self-portraits by Rembrandt">Rembrandt\'s self-portrait</a> as an oriental potentate with a <a href="/wiki/Kris" title="Kris">kris</a>/<a href="/wiki/Keris" class="mw-redirect" title="Keris">keris</a>, a Javanese blade weapon from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company_in_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch East India Company in Indonesia">VOC era</a> (etching, c. 1634). Also, he was one of the first known western <a href="/wiki/Printmaker" class="mw-redirect" title="Printmaker">printmakers</a> to extensively use (the VOC-imported) <a href="/wiki/Japanese_paper" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese paper">Japanese paper</a>. It\'s important to note that some major figures of Dutch Golden Age art like Rembrandt and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vermeer" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Vermeer">Vermeer</a> never went abroad during their lifetime. More than a pure for-profit corporation, the VOC was instrumental in \'bringing\' <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">the East</a> (<a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">Orient</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">the West</a> (<a href="/wiki/Occident" class="mw-redirect" title="Occident">Occident</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg/170px-Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg" width="170" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg/255px-Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg/340px-Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3245" data-file-height="3937" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willem_Kalf_-_Still-Life_with_a_Late_Ming_Ginger_Jar_-_WGA12080.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Still_Life_with_a_Chinese_Porcelain_Jar" title="Still Life with a Chinese Porcelain Jar">Still Life with a Chinese Porcelain Jar</a></i>, by Dutch Golden Age painter <a href="/wiki/Willem_Kalf" title="Willem Kalf">Willem Kalf</a> (c. 1660s). 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Chinese_export_porcelain" title="Chinese export porcelain">Chinese export porcelain</a> wares (imported by the VOC) are often depicted in many Dutch Golden Age <a href="/wiki/Genre_painting" title="Genre painting">genre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Still-life" class="mw-redirect" title="Still-life">still-life</a> paintings.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Delftware_display.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Delftware_display.JPG/170px-Delftware_display.JPG" width="170" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Delftware_display.JPG/255px-Delftware_display.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Delftware_display.JPG/340px-Delftware_display.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2531" data-file-height="1696" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Delftware_display.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shop window display of <a href="/wiki/Delftware" title="Delftware">Delftware</a> in the market place, <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a>. <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">East Asian-inspired</a> Delftware, a lasting cultural and economic legacy of the VOC era.</div></div></div> \n<p>From 1609 the VOC had a trading post in Japan (<a href="/wiki/Hirado,_Nagasaki" title="Hirado, Nagasaki">Hirado, Nagasaki</a>), which used local paper for its own administration. However, the paper was also traded to the VOC\'s other trading posts and even the Dutch Republic. Many impressions of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">Dutch Golden Age artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>\'s prints were done on Japanese paper. From about 1647 Rembrandt sought increasingly to introduce variation into his prints by using different sorts of paper, and printed most of his plates regularly on Japanese paper. He also used the paper for <a href="/wiki/List_of_drawings_by_Rembrandt" title="List of drawings by Rembrandt">his drawings</a>. The Japanese paper types \xe2\x80\x93 which was actually imported from Japan by the VOC \xe2\x80\x93 attracted Rembrandt with its warm, yellowish colour.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> They are often smooth and shiny, whilst Western paper has a more rough and matt surface.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, the VOC\'s imported <a href="/wiki/Chinese_export_porcelain" title="Chinese export porcelain">Chinese export porcelain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_export_porcelain" title="Japanese export porcelain">Japanese export porcelain</a> wares are <a href="/wiki/Chinese_porcelain_in_European_painting" title="Chinese porcelain in European painting">often depicted</a> in many Dutch Golden Age <a href="/wiki/Genre_painting" title="Genre painting">genre paintings</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vermeer" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Vermeer">Jan Vermeer</a>\'s paintings.<sup id="cite_ref-TimothyBrook_34-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimothyBrook-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Contributions in the Age of Exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Maritime_history_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Maritime history of the Dutch East India Company">Category:Maritime history of the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Dutch_Republic_in_the_Age_of_Discovery" title="Category:Dutch Republic in the Age of Discovery">Category:Dutch Republic in the Age of Discovery</a>, <a Maior</a></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">(...) The Dutch polity of the seventeenth century was famously unconcerned with territorial expansion: as long as the frontier operated effectively as a defensive shield, no extra land was deemed necessary.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Peter_J._Taylor" title="Peter J. Taylor">Peter J. Taylor</a>, in "World City Network: A Global Urban Analysis" (2004)<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nova_et_Accuratissima_Terrarum_Orbis_Tabula_(J.Blaeu,_1664).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" 2x" data-file-width="7686" data-file-height="6751" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nova_et_Accuratissima_Terrarum_Orbis_Tabula_(J.Blaeu,_1664).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blaeu\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Atlas_Maior" title="Atlas Maior">Atlas Maior</a></i> (1662\xe2\x80\x931672), a monumental multi-volume <a href="/wiki/World_atlas" class="mw-redirect" title="World atlas">world atlas</a> from the Golden Age of Dutch/Netherlandish cartography (c. 1570s\xe2\x80\x931670s) and a widely recognized masterpiece in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_cartography" title="History of cartography">history of mapmaking</a>. <a href="/wiki/Willem_Blaeu" title="Willem Blaeu">Willem Blaeu</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Joan_Blaeu" title="Joan Blaeu">Joan Blaeu</a> were both official cartographers to the VOC.</div></div></div> \n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg/170px-Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg.png" width="170" height="98" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg/255px-Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg/340px-Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oceania_UN_Geoscheme_-_Map_of_Melanesia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regions of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a>). "The Island Continent" <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">Australia</a> was the last human-inhabited continent to be largely known to the <a href="/wiki/Civilized_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Civilized world">civilized world</a>. The VOC\'s navigators were the first non-natives to undisputedly discover, explore and chart coastlines of <a href="/wiki/European_maritime_exploration_of_Australia" title="European maritime exploration of Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tasmania" title="History of Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tonga" title="History of Tonga">Tonga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Fiji" title="History of Fiji">Fiji</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tasmanroutes.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tasmanroutes.PNG/170px-Tasmanroutes.PNG" width="170" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tasmanroutes.PNG/255px-Tasmanroutes.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Tasmanroutes.PNG/340px-Tasmanroutes.PNG 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="455" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tasmanroutes.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>\'s routes of the first and second voyage</div></div></div>\n<p>The Dutch East India Company (VOC) was also a major force behind the <a href="/wiki/Category:Dutch_Republic_in_the_Age_of_Discovery" title="Category:Dutch Republic in the Age of Discovery">Golden Age of Dutch exploration and discovery</a> (c. 1590s\xe2\x80\x931720s). The VOC-funded exploratory voyages such as those led by <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Duyfken" title="Duyfken">Duyfken</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> revealed largely unknown landmasses to the civilized world. Also, during the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Netherlandish_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography">Golden Age of Dutch/Netherlandish cartography</a> (c. 1570s\xe2\x80\x931670s), VOC navigators, explorers, and cartographers<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;ae&#93;</a></sup> helped shape cartographic and geographic knowledge of the modern-day world.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Halve_Maen.27s_exploratory_voyage_and_role_in_the_formation_of_New_Netherland"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Halve_Maen\'s_exploratory_voyage_and_role_in_the_formation_of_New_Netherland"><i>Halve Maen\'</i>s exploratory voyage and role in the formation of New Netherland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Halve Maen&#039;s exploratory voyage and role in the formation of New Netherland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_(state)" title="History of New York (state)">History of New York (state)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_City" title="History of New York City">History of New York City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">History of North America</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg/180px-Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg" width="180" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg/270px-Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg/360px-Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3480" data-file-height="2088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Halve_Maen_approaching_Manhattan_28_June_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A replica of the VOC\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a></i> (captained by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a>, an Englishman in the service of the Dutch Republic) passes modern-day lower <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, where the original ship would have sailed while investigating <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_City" title="History of New York City">New York</a> harbor</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1609, English sea captain and <a href="/wiki/Explorer" class="mw-redirect" title="Explorer">explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> was hired by the VOC \xc3\xa9migr\xc3\xa9s running the VOC located in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a><sup id="cite_ref-brusselsjournal.com_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsjournal.com-316">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> to find a <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Passage" title="Northeast Passage">north-east passage</a> to Asia, sailing around Scandinavia and Russia. He was turned back by the ice of the Arctic in his second attempt, so he sailed west to seek a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">north-west passage</a> rather than return home. He ended up exploring the waters off the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">east coast</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/Flyboat" title="Flyboat">vlieboot</a></i> <i><a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a></i>. His first landfall was at <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> and the second at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">Cape Cod</a>.\n</p><p>Hudson believed that the passage to the Pacific Ocean was between the <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a>, so he sailed south to the Bay then turned northward, traveling close along the shore. He first discovered Delaware Bay and began to sail upriver looking for the passage. This effort was foiled by sandy shoals, and the <i>Halve Maen</i> continued north. After passing <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Hook" title="Sandy Hook">Sandy Hook</a>, Hudson and his crew entered the <a href="/wiki/The_Narrows" title="The Narrows">narrows</a> into the Upper New York Bay. (Unbeknownst to Hudson, the narrows had already been discovered in 1524 by explorer <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a>; today, the bridge spanning them is named after him.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>) Hudson believed that he had found the continental water route, so he sailed up the major river which later bore his name: the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson</a>. He found the water too shallow to proceed several days later, at the site of present-day <a href="/wiki/Troy,_New_York" title="Troy, New York">Troy, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Upon returning to the Netherlands, Hudson reported that he had found a fertile land and an amicable people willing to engage his crew in small-scale bartering of furs, trinkets, clothes, and small manufactured goods. His report was first published in 1611 by <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Van_Meteren" class="mw-redirect" title="Emanuel Van Meteren">Emanuel Van Meteren</a>, an Antwerp \xc3\xa9migr\xc3\xa9 and the Dutch Consul at London.<sup id="cite_ref-brusselsjournal.com_316-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brusselsjournal.com-316">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> This stimulated interest<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> in exploiting this new trade resource, and it was the catalyst for Dutch merchant-traders to fund more expeditions.\n</p><p>In 1611\xe2\x80\x9312, the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_of_Amsterdam" title="Admiralty of Amsterdam">Admiralty of Amsterdam</a> sent two covert expeditions to find a passage to <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> with the yachts <i>Craen</i> and <i>Vos</i>, captained by Jan Cornelisz Mey and Symon Willemsz Cat, respectively. In four voyages made between 1611 and 1614, the area between present-day <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> was explored, surveyed, and charted by <a href="/wiki/Adriaen_Block" title="Adriaen Block">Adriaen Block</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Christiaensen" title="Hendrick Christiaensen">Hendrick Christiaensen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Jacobsen_Mey" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornelius Jacobsen Mey">Cornelius Jacobsen Mey</a>. The results of these explorations, surveys, and charts made from 1609 through 1614 were consolidated in Block\'s map, which used the name <i><a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a></i> for the first time.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Dutch_discovery.2C_exploration.2C_and_mapping_of_mainland_Australia.2C_Tasmania.2C_New_Zealand.2C_and_various_islands"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_discovery,_exploration,_and_mapping_of_mainland_Australia,_Tasmania,_New_Zealand,_and_various_islands">Dutch discovery, exploration, and mapping of mainland Australia, Tasmania, New Zealand, and various islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Dutch discovery, exploration, and mapping of mainland Australia, Tasmania, New Zealand, and various islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Janszoon_voyage_of_1605%E2%80%9306" title="Janszoon voyage of 1605\xe2\x80\x9306">Janszoon voyage of 1605\xe2\x80\x9306</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brouwer_Route" title="Brouwer Route">Brouwer Route</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartog_Plate" title="Hartog Plate">Hartog Plate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_places_with_Dutch_names" title="Australian places with Dutch names">Australian places with Dutch names</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_exploration_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch exploration of Australia">Dutch exploration of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">New Holland (Australia)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen&#39;s Land">Van Diemen\'s Land</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Zeelandia" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Zeelandia">Nova Zeelandia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Pacific" title="Exploration of the Pacific">Exploration of the Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia" title="History of Australia">History of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="History of the Northern Territory">History of the Northern Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_Australia" title="History of Western Australia">History of Western Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Australia" title="History of South Australia">History of South Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tasmania" title="History of Tasmania">History of Tasmania</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">History of New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Fiji" title="History of Fiji">History of Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tonga" title="History of Tonga">History of Tonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">History of Oceania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vries_Strait" title="Vries Strait">Vries Strait</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png/180px-Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png" width="180" height="143" class="thumbimage" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png/360px-Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png 2x" data-file-width="2916" data-file-height="2310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical map from the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Dutch_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Dutch cartography">Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography</a>. <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a> during the Golden Age of Dutch exploration and discovery (c. 1590s\xe2\x80\x931720s): including <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea#History" title="New Guinea">Nova Guinea</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>), <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">Nova Hollandia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mainland_Australia" title="Mainland Australia">mainland Australia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen&#39;s Land">Van Diemen\'s Land</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Nova_Zeelandia" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Zeelandia">Nova Zeelandia</a> (<a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png/180px-Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png" width="180" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png/270px-Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png/360px-Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1105" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Australia_discoveries_by_Europeans_before_1813_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">Nova Hollandia</a>) was the last human-inhabited <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> to be explored and mapped (by non-natives). The Dutch were <a href="/wiki/Janszoon_voyage_of_1605%E2%80%9306" title="Janszoon voyage of 1605\xe2\x80\x9306">the first to undisputedly explore and map Australia\'s coastline</a>. In the 17th century, the VOC\'s navigators and explorers <a href="/wiki/Dutch_exploration_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch exploration of Australia">charted almost three-quarters of the Australian coastline</a>, except the east coast.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius,_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png/180px-Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png" width="180" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png/270px-Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png/360px-Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius%2C_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png 2x" data-file-width="684" data-file-height="532" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Detail_of_1657_map_Polus_Antarcticus_by_Jan_Janssonius,_showing_Nova_Zeelandia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail from a 1657 map by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Janssonius" title="Jan Janssonius">Jan Janssonius</a>, showing the western coastline of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Zeelandia" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Zeelandia">Nova Zeelandia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In terms of world history of geography and exploration, the VOC can be credited with putting most of Australia\'s coast (then Hollandia Nova and other names) on the world map, between 1606 and 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>\nWhile Australia\'s territory (originally known as <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">New Holland</a>) never became an actual Dutch settlement or colony,<sup id="cite_ref-Peter_J_2002_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_J_2002-61">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Dutch navigators were the first to undisputedly explore and map Australian coastline. In the 17th century, the VOC\'s navigators and explorers charted almost three-quarters of Australia\'s coastline, except its east coast. The Dutch ship, <i><a href="/wiki/Duyfken" title="Duyfken">Duyfken</a></i>, led by <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a>, made the first documented European landing in Australia in 1606.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Although a <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_the_Portuguese_discovery_of_Australia" title="Theory of the Portuguese discovery of Australia">theory of Portuguese discovery</a> in the 1520s exists, it lacks definitive evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> Precedence of discovery has also been claimed for <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Menzies_2002_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Menzies_2002-330">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Brosses_note_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brosses_note-331">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hargraves_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hargraves-332">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tamils_spread_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamils_spread-333">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> and even <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robinson_1980_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson_1980-334">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Brouwer" title="Hendrik Brouwer">Hendrik Brouwer</a>\'s discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Brouwer_Route" title="Brouwer Route">Brouwer Route</a>, that sailing east from the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> until land was sighted and then sailing north along the west coast of Australia was a much quicker route than around the coast of the Indian Ocean, made Dutch landfalls on the west coast inevitable. The first such landfall was in 1616, when <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Hartog" title="Dirk Hartog">Dirk Hartog</a> landed at Cape Inscription on what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Hartog_Island" title="Dirk Hartog Island">Dirk Hartog Island</a>, off the coast of Western Australia, and left behind an inscription on a <a href="/wiki/Pewter" title="Pewter">pewter</a> <a href="/wiki/Hartog_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hartog plate">plate</a>. In 1697 the Dutch captain <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Vlamingh" title="Willem de Vlamingh">Willem de Vlamingh</a> landed on the island and discovered <a href="/wiki/Hartog_Plate" title="Hartog Plate">Hartog\'s plate</a>. He replaced it with one of his own, which included a copy of Hartog\'s inscription, and took the original plate home to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, where it is still kept in the <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Rijksmuseum Amsterdam">Rijksmuseum Amsterdam</a>.\n</p><p>In 1627, the VOC\'s explorers <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Thijssen" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Nuyts" title="Pieter Nuyts">Pieter Nuyts</a> discovered the south coast of Australia and charted about 1,800 kilometres (1,100&#160;mi) of it between <a href="/wiki/Cape_Leeuwin" title="Cape Leeuwin">Cape Leeuwin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nuyts_Archipelago" title="Nuyts Archipelago">Nuyts Archipelago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foundation_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation-336">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Thijssen" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen</a>, captain of the ship <i><a href="/wiki/%27t_Gulden_Zeepaert" class="mw-redirect" title="&#39;t Gulden Zeepaert">\'t Gulden Zeepaert</a></i> (The Golden Seahorse), sailed to the east as far as <a href="/wiki/Ceduna" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceduna">Ceduna</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>. The first known ship to have visited the area is the <i>Leeuwin</i> ("Lioness"), a Dutch vessel that charted some of the nearby coastline in 1622. The log of the <i>Leeuwin</i> has been lost, so very little is known of the voyage. However, the land discovered by the <i>Leeuwin</i> was recorded on a 1627 map by <a href="/wiki/Hessel_Gerritsz" title="Hessel Gerritsz">Hessel Gerritsz</a>: <a href="/wiki/Caert_van%27t_Landt_van_d%27Eendracht" title="Caert van&#39;t Landt van d&#39;Eendracht">Caert van\'t Landt van d\'Eendracht</a> ("Chart of the Land of Eendracht"), which appears to show the coast between present-day <a href="/wiki/Hamelin_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamelin Bay">Hamelin Bay</a> and Point D\xe2\x80\x99Entrecasteaux. Part of Thijssen\'s map shows the islands St Francis and St Peter, now known collectively with their respective groups as the <a href="/wiki/Nuyts_Archipelago" title="Nuyts Archipelago">Nuyts Archipelago</a>. Thijssen\'s observations were included as soon as 1628 by the VOC cartographer <a href="/wiki/Hessel_Gerritsz" title="Hessel Gerritsz">Hessel Gerritsz</a> in a chart of the Indies and New Holland. This voyage defined most of the southern coast of Australia and discouraged the notion that "<a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">New Holland</a>" as it was then known, was linked to Antarctica.\n</p><p>In 1642, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> sailed from <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and on 24 November, sighted <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>. He named Tasmania <a href="/wiki/Anthoonij_van_Diemenslandt" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthoonij van Diemenslandt">Anthoonij van Diemenslandt</a> (Anglicised as <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen&#39;s Land">Van Diemen\'s Land</a>), after <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Diemen" title="Anthony van Diemen">Anthony van Diemen</a>, the VOC\'s Governor General, who had commissioned his voyage.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> It was officially renamed <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> in honour of its first European discoverer on 1 January 1856.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1642, during the same expedition, Tasman\'s crew discovered and charted <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>\'s coastline. They were the first Europeans known to reach New Zealand. Tasman anchored at the northern end of the <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bay" title="Golden Bay">Golden Bay</a> (he named it <a href="/wiki/Murderers%27_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Murderers&#39; Bay">Murderers\' Bay</a>) in December 1642 and sailed northward to <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> following a clash with local M\xc4\x81ori. Tasman sketched sections of the two main islands\' west coasts. Tasman called them <i><a href="/wiki/Staten_Landt" class="mw-redirect" title="Staten Landt">Staten Landt</a></i>, after the <i><a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General of the Netherlands</a></i>, and that name appeared on his first maps of the country. In 1645 Dutch cartographers changed the name to <i><a href="/wiki/Nova_Zeelandia" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Zeelandia">Nova Zeelandia</a></i> in Latin, from <i>Nieuw Zeeland</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Dutch province</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Zeeland" title="Zeeland">Zeeland</a></i>. It was subsequently Anglicised as <i>New Zealand</i> by <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>. Various claims have been made that New Zealand was reached by other non-<a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> voyagers before Tasman, but these are not widely accepted.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC-sponsored_inland_exploration_and_mapping_of_Southern_Africa">VOC-sponsored inland exploration and mapping of Southern Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: VOC-sponsored inland exploration and mapping of Southern Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa" title="History of South Africa">History of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Dutch Cape Colony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namaqualand" title="Namaqualand">Namaqualand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_van_der_Stel" title="Simon van der Stel">Simon van der Stel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_van_Rheede" title="Hendrik van Rheede">Hendrik van Rheede</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaq_Schrijver" title="Isaq Schrijver">Isaq Schrijver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Levaillant" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Levaillant">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Levaillant</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jacob_Gordon" title="Robert Jacob Gordon">Robert Jacob Gordon</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">Dodo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_capitalism" title="Criticism of capitalism">Criticism of capitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Criticisms_of_globalization" title="Criticisms of globalization">Criticisms of globalization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corporate_crime" title="Corporate crime">Corporate crime</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/170px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/255px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/340px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2096" data-file-height="2240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The VOC\'s economic activity in <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> largely contributed to the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, a flightless bird that was endemic to the island. The first recorded mention of the dodo was by Dutch navigators in the late 1590s.</div></div></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">One of the paradoxes of the Company [VOC] is that the Dutch were <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">the most liberal and humane nation in Europe at that time</a>, and yet they created in the Company a very efficient monstrosity. It should not be forgotten that the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Netherlands at the time</a> was a newly independent nation, in true existential peril from <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">their former Spanish masters</a>, who committed a number of atrocities on Dutch soil. In this situation the Netherlands needed the huge monopoly profits promised by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieterszoon_Coen" title="Jan Pieterszoon Coen">Jan Pieterszoon Coen</a>\'s vision for the Company, which entailed not only shutting out other European powers with violence, but even dominating trade among the Asians themselves.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;VOC scholar <a href="/wiki/Graham_Harman" title="Graham Harman">Graham Harman</a>, 2016<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In spite of the VOC\'s historic successes and contributions, the Company has long been criticized for its quasi-absolute commercial <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopoly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">exploitation</a> (including use of <a href="/wiki/Slave_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave labour">slave labour</a>), <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>, use of violence, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_destruction" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental destruction">environmental destruction</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>), and overly <a href="/wiki/Bureaucratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Bureaucratic">bureaucratic</a> in organizational structure.<sup id="cite_ref-RussellShorto_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RussellShorto-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="VOC_colonialism.2C_monopoly_policy_and_uses_of_violence"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_colonialism,_monopoly_policy_and_uses_of_violence">VOC colonialism, monopoly policy and uses of violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: VOC colonialism, monopoly policy and uses of violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(August 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:Military_history_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Military history of the Dutch East India Company">Military history of the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Battles_involving_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Battles involving the Dutch East India Company">Battles involving the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="European colonization of Africa">European colonization of Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_imperialism_in_Asia" title="Western imperialism in Asia">Western imperialism in Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_Southeast_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="European colonization of Southeast Asia">European colonization of Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Spice wars">Spice wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amboyna_massacre" title="Amboyna massacre">Amboyna massacre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Batavia_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Batavia massacre">Batavia massacre</a></div>\n<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9c\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Your Honours know by experience that trade in Asia must be driven and maintained under the protection and favour of Your Honours\' own weapons, and that the weapons must be paid for by the profits from the trade; so that we cannot carry on trade without war nor war without trade.\n</td>\n<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">\xe2\x80\x9d\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<a href="/wiki/Jan_Pieterszoon_Coen" title="Jan Pieterszoon Coen">Jan Pieterszoon Coen</a>, the VOC\'s <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief executive">chief executive</a> [in the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>], to the <a href="/wiki/Heeren_XVII" class="mw-redirect" title="Heeren XVII">Heeren XVII</a>, the VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> [in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>], in 1614<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_slave_trade_and_slavery_under_the_VOC_colonial_rule">Dutch slave trade and slavery under the VOC colonial rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Dutch slave trade and slavery under the VOC colonial rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery" title="History of slavery">History of slavery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_South_Africa" title="Slavery in South Africa">Slavery in South Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Meermin_slave_mutiny" title="Meermin slave mutiny">Meermin slave mutiny</a></div>\n<p>By the time the settlement was established at the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Cape</a> in 1652, the VOC already had a long experience of practising <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> in the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck" title="Jan van Riebeeck">Jan van Riebeeck</a> concluded within two months of the establishment of the Cape settlement that <a href="/wiki/Slave_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave labor">slave labor</a> would be needed for the hardest and dirtiest work. Initially, the VOC considered enslaving men from the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi" title="Khoikhoi">Khoikhoi</a> population, but the idea was rejected on the grounds that such a policy would be both costly and dangerous. Most Khoikhoi had chosen not to labor for the Dutch because of low wages and harsh conditions. In the beginning, the settlers traded with the Khoikhoi but the harsh working conditions and low wages imposed by the Dutch led to a series of wars. The European population remained under 200 during the settlement\'s first five years, and war against neighbors numbering more than 20,000 would have been foolhardy. Moreover, the Dutch feared that Khoikhoi people, if enslaved, could always escape into the local community, whereas foreigners would find it much more difficult to elude their "masters."<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes-slave-economy_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes-slave-economy-344">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1652 and 1657, a number of unsuccessful attempts were made to obtain men from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> and from <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>. In 1658, however, the VOC landed two shiploads of slaves at the Cape, one containing more than 200 people brought from <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">Dahomey</a> (later Benin), the second with almost 200 people, most of them children, captured from a Portuguese slaver off the coast of Angola. Except for a few individuals, these were to be the only slaves ever brought to the Cape from West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes-slave-economy_344-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes-slave-economy-344">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> From 1658 to the end of the Company\'s rule, many more slaves were brought regularly to the Cape in various ways, chiefly by Company-sponsored slaving voyages and slaves brought to the Cape by its return fleets. From these sources and by natural growth, the slave population increased from zero in 1652 to about 1,000 by 1700. During the 18th century, the slave population increased dramatically to 16,839 by 1795. After the slave trade was initiated, all of the slaves imported into the Cape until the British stopped the trade in 1807 were from East Africa, Mozambique, Madagascar, and South and Southeast Asia. Large numbers were brought from India, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Ceylon</a>, and the Indonesian archipelago. Prisoners from other countries in the VOC\'s empire were also enslaved. The slave population, which exceeded that of the European settlers until the first quarter of the nineteenth century, was overwhelmingly male and was thus dependent on constant imports of new slaves to maintain and to augment its size.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes-slave-economy_344-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes-slave-economy-344">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the 1660s the Cape settlement was importing slaves from India, Malaya (Malaysia), and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> to work on the farms.<sup id="cite_ref-Appiah_p732_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Appiah_p732-345">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Conflict between Dutch farmers and Khoikhoi broke out once it became clear to the latter that the Dutch were there to stay and that they intended to encroach on the lands of the pastoralists. In 1659 Doman, a Khoikhoi who had worked as a translator for the Dutch and had even traveled to Java, led an armed attempt to expel the Dutch from the Cape peninsula. The attempt was a failure, although warfare dragged on until an inconclusive peace was established a year later. During the following decade, pressure on the Khoikhoi grew as more of the Dutch became free burghers, expanded their landholdings, and sought pastureland for their growing herds. War broke out again in 1673 and continued until 1677, when Khoikhoi resistance was destroyed by a combination of superior European weapons and Dutch manipulation of divisions among the local people. Thereafter, Khoikhoi society in the western Cape disintegrated. Some people found jobs as shepherds on European farms; others rejected foreign rule and moved away from the Cape. The final blow for most came in 1713 when a Dutch ship brought smallpox to the Cape. Hitherto unknown locally, the disease ravaged the remaining Khoikhoi, killing 90 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes-slave-economy_344-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes-slave-economy-344">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> Throughout the eighteenth century, the settlement continued to expand through internal growth of the European population and the continued importation of slaves. The approximately 3,000 Europeans and slaves at the Cape in 1700 had increased by the end of the century to nearly 20,000 Europeans, and approximately 25,000 slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrnes-slave-economy_344-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrnes-slave-economy-344">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_depictions_of_people_and_things_associated_with_the_VOC">Cultural depictions of people and things associated with the VOC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span with the VOC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_works_about_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="List of works about the Dutch East India Company">List of works about the Dutch East India Company</a></div>\n<div class="thumb Petersburg, Russia">St. Petersburg, Russia</a>. In order to learn more about the 17th-century Dutch maritime superpower,<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;af&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Tsar Peter I <a href="/wiki/Grand_Embassy_of_Peter_the_Great" title="Grand Embassy of Peter the Great">came to work incognito</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Shipwright" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipwright">ship\'s carpenter</a> at the VOC\'s shipyards in Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a>/Saardam, for a period of four months (1697).</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Batavia_(ship)" title="Batavia (ship)">Batavia</a></i>: a shipwreck on the <a href="/wiki/Houtman_Abrolhos" title="Houtman Abrolhos">Houtman Abrolhos</a> in 1629, made famous by the subsequent mutiny and massacre that took place among the survivors. [see also <i><a href="/wiki/Batavia_(opera)" title="Batavia (opera)">Batavia</a></i> (opera)]</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Flying_Dutchman" title="Flying Dutchman">Flying Dutchman</a></i>: a legendary <a href="/wiki/Ghost_ship" title="Ghost ship">ghost ship</a> in several maritime myths, likely to have originated from the 17th-century golden age of the VOC.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hansken" title="Hansken">Hansken</a></i>: a female <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a> from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Dutch Ceylon</a>. The young elephant <i>Hansken</i> was brought to Amsterdam in 1637, aboard a VOC ship. Dutch Golden Age artist <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a> made some historical drawings of <i>Hansken</i>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia, Dutch East Indies</a></i>: 1650s/1660s paintings of scenes from everyday life by <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">Dutch Golden Age painter</a> <a href="/wiki/Andries_Beeckman" title="Andries Beeckman">Andries Beeckman</a>, one of the few painters who travelled to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> in the 17th century.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Cosmos:_A_Personal_Voyage" title="Cosmos: A Personal Voyage">Cosmos: A Personal Voyage</a></i>: in the 6th episode <i><a href="/wiki/Travellers%27_Tales" class="mw-redirect" title="Travellers&#39; Tales">Travellers\' Tales</a></i> of the popular documentary TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmos:_A_Personal_Voyage" title="Cosmos: A Personal Voyage">Cosmos</a></i> (1980), American astronomer <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a>, who also served as host, took a look at the voyage to Jupiter and Saturn, and compared these events with the adventuring spirit of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age" title="Dutch Golden Age">Dutch Golden Age</a> explorers (including the VOC\'s navigators).</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Sino-Dutch_War_1661" title="The Sino-Dutch War 1661">The Sino-Dutch War 1661</a></i>: 2000 Chinese historical drama film. The film is loosely based on the life of <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> (<a href="/wiki/Zheng_Chenggong" class="mw-redirect" title="Zheng Chenggong">Zheng Chenggong</a>) and focuses on his battle with the VOC for control of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Dutch Formosa</a> at the Siege of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Zeelandia_(Taiwan)" title="Fort Zeelandia (Taiwan)">Fort Zeelandia</a>.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ocean%27s_Twelve" title="Ocean&#39;s Twelve">Ocean\'s Twelve</a></i>: a 2004 American comedy heist film inspired by the historical story from the VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/IPO" class="mw-redirect" title="IPO">IPO</a> and the first shares of stock ever traded publicly in history. The VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Stock_certificate" title="Stock certificate">stock certificate</a> is the focused heist by the burglars in the movie.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Thousand_Autumns_of_Jacob_de_Zoet" title="The Thousand Autumns of Jacob de Zoet">The Thousand Autumns of Jacob de Zoet</a></i>, 2010 historical novel by British author <a href="/wiki/David_Mitchell_(author)" title="David Mitchell (author)">David Mitchell</a>.</li>\n<li><i>My Father\'s Islands: Abel Tasman\'s Heroic Voyages</i>: a 2012 <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_fiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Juvenile fiction">juvenile fiction</a> by Christobel Mattingley, written from the perspective of <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Tasman</a>\'s young daughter, Claesgen. The fictional story was inspired by a 1637 painting of the Tasman family by the Dutch Golden Age painter <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Gerritsz._Cuyp" title="Jacob Gerritsz. Cuyp">Jacob Gerritsz. Cuyp</a>, one of the treasures of the National Library of Australia.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">The Tsar-Carpenter</a></i>: a cultural depiction of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Tsar" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Tsar">Tsar</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> (<a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter I of Russia">Peter I of Russia</a>) in his undercover visit to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Embassy_of_Peter_the_Great" title="Grand Embassy of Peter the Great">Grand Embassy</a> mission (1697\xe2\x80\x931698). When Peter the Great wanted to learn more about the Dutch Republic\'s <a href="/wiki/Sea_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea power">sea power</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> he came to study <a href="/wiki/Seamanship" title="Seamanship">seamanship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipbuilding industry">shipbuilding industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpentry" title="Carpentry">carpentry</a> in Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/Czar_Peter_House_(Netherlands)" title="Czar Peter House (Netherlands)">Zaandam</a> (Saardam).<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;ag&#93;</a></sup> Through the agency of <a href="/wiki/Nicolaas_Witsen" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolaas Witsen">Nicolaas Witsen</a>, mayor of Amsterdam and an expert on Russia, Tsar Peter I worked as a <a href="/wiki/Shipwright" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipwright">ship\'s carpenter</a> in the VOC\'s <a href="/wiki/Shipyards" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipyards">shipyards</a> in <a href="/wiki/Holland" title="Holland">Holland</a>. [see also <i><a href="/wiki/Zar_und_Zimmermann" title="Zar und Zimmermann">Zar und Zimmermann</a></i> (opera) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Czar_and_the_Carpenter" title="The Czar and the Carpenter">The Czar and the Carpenter</a></i> (film)]</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Megacorporation" title="Megacorporation">Megacorporation</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Mega-corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mega-corporation">mega-corporation</a></i>: a quasi-fictional term/concept derived from the combination of the prefix <i><a href="/wiki/Mega-" title="Mega-">mega-</a></i> with the word <i><a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">corporation</a></i>, possibly inspired by the VOC\'s history. It refers to a (quasi-fictional) corporation that is a massive <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a>, possessing quasi-governmental powers and holding <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">monopolistic</a> control over markets.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Black_swan_theory" title="Black swan theory">Black swan theory</a></i>: a <a href="/wiki/Metaphor" title="Metaphor">metaphor</a> or metatheory of science popularized by <a href="/wiki/Nassim_Nicholas_Taleb" title="Nassim Nicholas Taleb">Nassim Nicholas Taleb</a>. It was possibly inspired by <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Vlamingh" title="Willem de Vlamingh">Willem de Vlamingh</a>\'s 1697 discovery. De Vlamingh was the first known European/Western to observe and describe <a href="/wiki/Black_swans" class="mw-redirect" title="Black swans">black swans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quokkas" class="mw-redirect" title="Quokkas">quokkas</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_World_etymologies">VOC World etymologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
