Zwaanenrivier / Swan River</a> (Australia), by Willem de Vlamingh</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Populated_places_established_by_VOC_people">Populated places established by VOC people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Populated places established by VOC people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg/170px-Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg" width="170" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg/255px-Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg/340px-Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moederkerk_Swellendam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cape_Dutch_architecture" title="Cape Dutch architecture">Cape Dutch style</a>-influenced eclectic building of the <a href="/wiki/Nederduitse_Gereformeerde_Kerk" class="mw-redirect" title="Nederduitse Gereformeerde Kerk">Nederduitse Gereformeerde Kerk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swellendam" title="Swellendam">Swellendam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cape_Dutch_architecture" title="Cape Dutch architecture">Cape Dutch architecture</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans_literature" title="Afrikaans literature">Afrikaans literature</a>, is among the lasting legacy of the VOC-era <a href="/wiki/Afrikaners" title="Afrikaners">Afrikaans culture</a> in South Africa.</div></div></div>\n<p>Populated places (including cities, towns and villages) established/founded<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;aj&#93;</a></sup> by people of the Dutch East India Company (VOC).\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>), modern-day <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">Jakarta</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tainan" title="Tainan">Tainan</a>, the oldest <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, located in southern-western Taiwan</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kaohsiung" title="Kaohsiung">Kaohsiung</a> (formerly known as Takao or <a href="/wiki/Dagao" class="mw-redirect" title="Dagao">Dagao</a>), located in southern-western Taiwan</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kaapstad" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaapstad">Kaapstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>), the oldest urban area in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and one of the first permanent European settlements in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Constantia,_Cape_Town" title="Constantia, Cape Town">Constantia</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Cape_Town_suburbs" title="List of Cape Town suburbs">Cape Town\'s suburb</a>) is considered one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Wine-producing_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Wine-producing region">wine-producing regions</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stellenbosch" title="Stellenbosch">Stellenbosch</a>, the second oldest urban area (town) in South Africa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swellendam" title="Swellendam">Swellendam</a>, the third oldest urban area (town) in South Africa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Graaff-Reinet" title="Graaff-Reinet">Graaff-Reinet</a>, the fourth oldest urban area (town) in South Africa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Franschhoek" title="Franschhoek">Franschhoek</a>, a town in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Cape Province">Western Cape Province</a>, South Africa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paarl" title="Paarl">Paarl</a>, the third oldest European settlement in South Africa and the largest town in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Winelands" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Winelands">Cape Winelands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Simonstad" class="mw-redirect" title="Simonstad">Simonstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/Simon%27s_Town" title="Simon&#39;s Town">Simon\'s Town</a>), a town near Cape Town, South Africa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">Dutch Mauritius</a>, the first permanent <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">human settlement</a> ever in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mauritius" title="History of Mauritius">Mauritius</a><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;ak&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Important_heritage_sites_in_the_VOC_World">Important heritage sites in the VOC World</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Malacca">Christ Church</a> (Malacca City, Malaysia); <a href="/wiki/Stadthuys" title="Stadthuys">Stadthuys</a> (Malacca City, Malaysia)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_archives_and_records">VOC archives and records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: VOC archives and records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The VOC\'s operations (trading posts and colonies) produced not only warehouses packed with spices, coffee, tea, textiles, porcelain and silk, but also shiploads of documents. Data on political, economic, cultural, religious, and social conditions spread over an enormous area circulated between the VOC establishments, the administrative centre of the trade in <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> (the Heeren XVII/Gentlemen Seventeen) in the Dutch Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> The VOC records are included in <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory of the World Register">Memory of the World Register</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_coinage">VOC coinage</span><span class="mw-headline" id="Field_of_VOC_World_studies">Field of VOC World studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Field of VOC World studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_works_about_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="List of works about the Dutch East India Company">List of works about the Dutch East India Company</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Historians_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Historians of the Dutch East India Company">Category:Historians of the Dutch East India Company</a></div>\n<p>The Dutch East India Company (VOC), as a historical transcontinental <a href="/wiki/Megacorporation" title="Megacorporation">company-state</a>, is one of the best expertly researched business enterprises in history. For almost 200 years of the Company\'s existence (1602\xe2\x80\x931800), the VOC had effectively transformed itself from a corporate entity into a state, an empire, or even a world in its own right.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> The VOC World (i.e. networks of people, places, things, activities, and events associated with the Dutch East India Company) has been the subject of a vast amount of literature, including works of fiction and non-fiction. VOC World studies (often included within a broader field of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">early-modern Dutch global world</a> studies) is an international <a href="/wiki/Multidisciplinary" class="mw-redirect" title="Multidisciplinary">multidisciplinary</a> field focused on social, cultural, religious, scientific, technological, economic, financial, business, maritime, military, political, legal, diplomatic activities, organization and administration of the VOC and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dutch_East_India_Company_trading_posts_and_settlements" title="List of Dutch East India Company trading posts and settlements">its colourful world</a>. As North &amp; Kaufmann (2014) notes, "the Dutch East India Company (VOC) has long attracted the attention of scholarship. Its lengthy history, widespread enterprises, and the survival of massive amounts of documentation \xe2\x80\x93 literally 1,200 meters of essays pertaining to the VOC may be found in the National Archives in The Hague, and many more documents are scattered in archives throughout Asia and in South Africa \xe2\x80\x93 have stimulated many works on economic and social history. Important publications have also appeared on the trade, shipping, institutional organization, and administration of the VOC. Much has also been learned about the VOC and Dutch colonial societies. Moreover, the TANAP (Towards a New Age of Partnership, 2000\xe2\x80\x932007) project has created momentum for research on the relationship between the VOC and indigenous societies. In contrast, the role of the VOC in cultural history and especially in the history of visual and material culture has not yet attracted comparable interest. To be sure, journals and other travel accounts (some even with illustrations) by soldiers, shippers, and VOC officials among others have been utilized as sources."<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> VOC scholarship is highly specialized in general, such as archaeological studies of the VOC World. Some of the notable <a href="/wiki/Category:Historians_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Historians of the Dutch East India Company">VOC historians/scholars</a> include <a href="/wiki/S._Arasaratnam" title="S. Arasaratnam">Sinnappah Arasaratnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bluss%C3%A9" title="Leonard Bluss\xc3\xa9">Leonard Bluss\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Borschberg" title="Peter Borschberg">Peter Borschberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ralph_Boxer" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Ralph Boxer">Charles Ralph Boxer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaap_R._Bruijn" title="Jaap R. Bruijn">Jaap R. Bruijn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Femme_Gaastra" title="Femme Gaastra">Femme Gaastra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Om_Prakash_(historian)" title="Om Prakash (historian)">Om Prakash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Worden" title="Nigel Worden">Nigel Worden</a>.\n</p><p>For scholarly works (books and articles) about the VOC world, see article section: <a href="/wiki/List_of_works_about_the_Dutch_East_India_Company#Non-fiction" title="List of works about the Dutch East India Company">List of works about the Dutch East India Company#Non-fiction</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_World_archaeology">VOC World archaeology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: VOC World archaeology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(July 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Historical_archaeology" title="Historical archaeology">Historical archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maritime_archaeology" title="Maritime archaeology">Maritime archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Underwater_archaeology" title="Underwater archaeology">Underwater archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipwrecks_of_Western_Australia" title="Shipwrecks of Western Australia">Shipwrecks of Western Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_17th-century_shipwrecks_in_Australia" title="List of 17th-century shipwrecks in Australia">List of 17th-century shipwrecks in Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company_coinage" title="Dutch East India Company coinage">Dutch East India Company coinage</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dutch_East_India_Company_trading_posts_and_settlements" title="List of Dutch East India Company trading posts and settlements">List of Dutch East India Company trading posts and settlements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Populated_places_established_by_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Populated places established by the Dutch East India Company">Category:Populated places established by the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Buildings_and_structures_associated_with_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Buildings and structures associated with the Dutch East India Company">Category:Buildings and structures associated with the Dutch East India Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Category:Ships_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Ships of the Dutch East India Company">Category:Ships of the Dutch East India Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Category:Former_properties_of_the_Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Category:Former properties of the Dutch East India Company">Category:Former properties of the Dutch East India Company</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_timeline_and_historical_firsts">VOC timeline and historical firsts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: VOC timeline and historical firsts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The publication of the <i><a href="/wiki/Theatrum_Orbis_Terrarum" title="Theatrum Orbis Terrarum">Theatrum Orbis Terrarum</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius" title="Abraham Ortelius">Abraham Ortelius</a> in 1570 marked the official beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Netherlandish_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography">Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography</a> (c. 1570s\xe2\x80\x931670s). In the <a href="/wiki/Category:Dutch_Republic_in_the_Age_of_Discovery" title="Category:Dutch Republic in the Age of Discovery">Golden Age of Dutch exploration and discovery</a> (c. 1590s\xe2\x80\x931720s), the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>\'s seafarers and explorers (including the VOC\'s navigators) became the first non-natives to undisputedly discover, explore and map coastlines of the <a href="/wiki/European_maritime_exploration_of_Australia" title="European maritime exploration of Australia">Australian continent</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Australia" title="Mainland Australia">Mainland Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tasmania" title="History of Tasmania">Tasmania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Australia" title="List of islands of Australia">their surrounding islands</a>), <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tonga" title="History of Tonga">Tonga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Fiji" title="History of Fiji">Fiji</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Proto-VOC_period_.28with_the_establishment_of_the_voorcompagnie.C3.ABn.2Fpre-companies.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Proto-VOC_period_(with_the_establishment_of_the_voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)">Proto-VOC period (with the establishment of the <i>voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</i>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Proto-VOC period (with the establishment of the voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>1579: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Utrecht" title="Union of Utrecht">Union of Utrecht</a> as the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Seven_United_Provinces" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the Seven United Provinces">Republic of the Seven United Provinces</a> (or the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>).</li>\n<li>1580: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> (1580\xe2\x80\x931640) by <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a> and Lord of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Netherlands" title="Spanish Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (<i>Heer der Nederlanden</i> in Dutch).</li>\n<li>1581: <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Abjuration" title="Act of Abjuration">Act of Abjuration</a>.</li>\n<li>1585: <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Antwerp" title="Fall of Antwerp">Fall of Antwerp</a>.</li>\n<li>1594\xe2\x80\x931598: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Compagnie_van_Verre" title="Compagnie van Verre">Compagnie van Verre</a>, one of the forerunners (or the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</a></i>) of the United East India Company (VOC).</li>\n<li>1595\xe2\x80\x931597: <a href="/wiki/History_of_cartography#Dutch_celestial_cartography_in_the_Age_of_Exploration" title="History of cartography">First systematic mapping of the far southern sky in history of celestial cartography</a> (<a href="/wiki/Category:Constellations_listed_by_Petrus_Plancius" title="Category:Constellations listed by Petrus Plancius">12 Dutch-created southern constellations</a>). In the <a href="/wiki/First_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="First Dutch Expedition to Indonesia">first Dutch expedition to the East Indies</a>, Dutch navigators <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Dirkszoon_Keyser" title="Pieter Dirkszoon Keyser">Pieter Dirkszoon Keyser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frederick_de_Houtman" title="Frederick de Houtman">Frederick de Houtman</a> introduced and listed the 12 new <a href="/wiki/Category:Southern_constellations" title="Category:Southern constellations">southern constellations</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Apus" title="Apus">Apus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chamaeleon" title="Chamaeleon">Chamaeleon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dorado" title="Dorado">Dorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grus_(constellation)" title="Grus (constellation)">Grus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrus" title="Hydrus">Hydrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indus_(constellation)" title="Indus (constellation)">Indus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musca" title="Musca">Musca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavo_(constellation)" title="Pavo (constellation)">Pavo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(constellation)" title="Phoenix (constellation)">Phoenix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triangulum_Australe" title="Triangulum Australe">Triangulum Australe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tucana" title="Tucana">Tucana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volans" title="Volans">Volans</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> These 12 southern constellations first appeared on a 35-cm diameter <a href="/wiki/Celestial_globe" title="Celestial globe">celestial globe</a> published in 1597/1598 in Amsterdam by <a href="/wiki/Petrus_Plancius" title="Petrus Plancius">Petrus Plancius</a> (one of the founders of the Dutch East India Company) and <a href="/wiki/Jodocus_Hondius" title="Jodocus Hondius">Jodocus Hondius</a>.</li>\n<li>1596: Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Willem_Barentsz" title="Willem Barentsz">Willem Barentsz</a> and his crew became the firsts to undisputedly discover and chart the <a href="/wiki/Svalbard_archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Svalbard archipelago">Svalbard archipelago</a> while searching for the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a> (<a href="/wiki/Northeast_Passage" title="Northeast Passage">Northeast Passage</a>) to the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>.</li>\n<li>1596: The publication of <a href="/wiki/Jan_Huygen_van_Linschoten" class="mw-redirect" title="Jan Huygen van Linschoten">Jan Huygen van Linschoten</a>\'s <i>Itinerario</i> in Amsterdam opened the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> world for the European geographical imagination.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> Van Linschoten is credited with publishing in Europe important classified information about Asian trade and navigation that was hidden by the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian great powers</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>).</li>\n<li>1598\xe2\x80\x931600: <a href="/wiki/Second_Dutch_Expedition_to_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Dutch Expedition to Indonesia">Second Dutch expedition to the East Indies</a>.</li>\n<li>1599\xe2\x80\x931602: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Brabantsche_Compagnie" title="Brabantsche Compagnie">Brabantsche Compagnie</a>, one of the forerunners (<i>voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</i>) of the United East India Company (VOC).</li>\n<li>1600: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> (1600\xe2\x80\x931874).</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="VOC_era_.28with_the_amalgamation_of_the_voorcompagnie.C3.ABn.2Fpre-companies.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="VOC_era_(with_the_amalgamation_of_the_voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)">VOC era (with the amalgamation of the <i>voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies</i>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dutch_East_India_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: VOC era (with the amalgamation of the voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn/pre-companies)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>1602: On March 20, the United <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a> Company/United <a href="/wiki/East_India" title="East India">East India</a> Company (Vereenigde Oost-Indische Compagnie, or VOC in Dutch), often referred to by the British as the Dutch East India Company, the world\'s first true <a href="/wiki/Transnational_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnational corporation">transnational corporation</a>, was originally established as a <a href="/wiki/Chartered_company" title="Chartered company">chartered company</a>. The Company was founded from a <a href="/wiki/States-General_of_the_Dutch_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="States-General of the Dutch Republic">government-directed</a> <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_(business)" title="Consolidation (business)">consolidation/amalgamation</a> of the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Voorcompagnie" title="Voorcompagnie">voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn</a></i> (or <i>pre-companies</i>). The VOC was the first <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> to get a fixed <a href="/wiki/Financial_capital" title="Financial capital">capital stock</a> and the first recorded (public) company ever to pay regular <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividends</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1603: <a href="/wiki/Jacob_van_Heemskerk" title="Jacob van Heemskerk">Van Heemskerck</a>\'s capture of Portuguese carrack <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(ship)" title="Santa Catarina (ship)">Santa Catarina</a>.</li>\n<li>1606: The first (undisputed) documented European sighting of and landing on the Australian continent (<a href="/wiki/New_Holland_(Australia)" title="New Holland (Australia)">Nova Hollandia</a>) by the VOC navigator <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a> aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/Duyfken" title="Duyfken">Duyfken</a></i>.</li>\n<li>1608\xe2\x80\x931825: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Coromandel" title="Dutch Coromandel">Dutch Coromandel</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1609\xe2\x80\x931621: <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Years%27_Truce" title="Twelve Years&#39; Truce">Twelve Years\' Truce</a>.</li>\n<li>1609: The VOC ship <i><a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">Halve Maen</a>\'</i>s exploratory voyage, a milestone in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_(state)" title="History of New York (state)">history of New York</a> (including <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_City" title="History of New York City">New York City</a>) and <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">North America</a>. English explorer <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a>, in the employ of the VOC, sailed the <i>Halve Maen</i> through the Narrows into Upper New York Bay. He was looking for a westerly passage to the Far East.</li>\n<li>1609: Dutch <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Grotius" title="Hugo Grotius">Hugo Grotius</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_Liberum" title="Mare Liberum">Mare Liberum</a></i>, a foundational treatise on modern international <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_sea" title="Law of the sea">law of the sea</a>, while being a counsel to the Dutch East India Company (VOC) over the seizing of the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(ship)" title="Santa Catarina (ship)">Santa Catarina Portuguese carrack</a> issue.</li>\n<li>1609: The first recorded <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a> dispute, took place on January 24 (1609) between the <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholders</a>/<a href="/wiki/Investor" title="Investor">investors</a> (most notably <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Le_Maire" title="Isaac Le Maire">Isaac Le Maire</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">directors</a> of the VOC.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1609: The first recorded <a href="/wiki/Short_seller" class="mw-redirect" title="Short seller">short seller</a> in history, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Le_Maire" title="Isaac Le Maire">Isaac Le Maire</a>, a sizeable shareholder of the VOC.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1609: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of Amsterdam">Bank of Amsterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdamsche_Wisselbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdamsche Wisselbank">Amsterdamsche Wisselbank</a> in Dutch), arguably the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>.</li>\n<li>1610: An early mechanism of <a href="/wiki/Financial_regulation" title="Financial regulation">financial regulation</a> practice was the first recorded ban on <a href="/wiki/Short_selling" class="mw-redirect" title="Short selling">short selling</a>, by the Dutch authorities.</li>\n<li>1611: The world\'s first official/formal <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>, or <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beurs_van_Hendrick_de_Keyser" class="extiw" title="nl:Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser">Beurs van Hendrick de Keyser</a> in Dutch) and <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> were launched by the VOC in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1611: The VOC was the first corporation to be ever actually <a href="/wiki/Listing_(finance)" title="Listing (finance)">listed</a> on an official/formal <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>. In other words, the VOC was the world\'s first formally <a href="/wiki/Listing_(finance)" title="Listing (finance)">listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public company</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Publicly_listed_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Publicly listed company">publicly listed company</a>).</li>\n<li>1611: Discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Brouwer_Route" title="Brouwer Route">Brouwer Route</a> by the VOC navigator <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Brouwer" title="Hendrik Brouwer">Hendrik Brouwer</a>.</li>\n<li>1616: The VOC navigator <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Hartog" title="Dirk Hartog">Dirk Hartog</a> made the first recorded European landing on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">west coast of the Australian continent</a>.</li>\n<li>1616: <a href="/wiki/Hartog_Plate" title="Hartog Plate">Hartog Plate</a>, the first known European artefact found on Australian soil (<a href="/wiki/Dirk_Hartog_Island" title="Dirk Hartog Island">Dirk Hartog Island</a>).</li>\n<li>1616\xe2\x80\x931825: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Suratte" title="Dutch Suratte">Dutch Suratte</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1616: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Danish East India Company</a> (1616\xe2\x80\x931729).</li>\n<li>1619: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> at the site of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">razed city of Jayakarta</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1619: <a href="/wiki/Batavia_Castle" title="Batavia Castle">Batavia Castle</a> (<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kasteel_van_Batavia" class="extiw" title="nl:Kasteel van Batavia">Kasteel van Batavia</a> in Dutch) was built by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1621: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> (WIC/GWIC in Dutch).</li>\n<li>1622: On January 24, Amsterdam-based businessman <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Le_Maire" title="Isaac Le Maire">Isaac Le Maire</a> filed a petition against the VOC, marking the first recorded expression of <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_activism" class="mw-redirect" title="Shareholder activism">shareholder activism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_rebellion" title="Shareholder rebellion">shareholder rebellion</a>.</li>\n<li>1623: <a href="/wiki/Amboyna_massacre" title="Amboyna massacre">Amboyna massacre</a>.</li>\n<li>1624\xe2\x80\x931634: <a href="/wiki/Fort_Zeelandia_(Taiwan)" title="Fort Zeelandia (Taiwan)">Fort Zeelandia</a>/<a href="/wiki/Anping_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Anping fort">Fort Anping</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Dutch Formosa</a>) was built by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1624\xe2\x80\x931662: <a href="/wiki/Tainan" title="Tainan">Tainan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Formosa" title="Dutch Formosa">Dutch Formosa</a>), the first <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> to be established in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Taiwan" title="History of Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.</li>\n<li>1627\xe2\x80\x931825: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Bengal" title="Dutch Bengal">Dutch Bengal</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1627: The VOC explorers <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Thijssen" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Thijssen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Nuyts" title="Pieter Nuyts">Pieter Nuyts</a> made the first recorded European landing on the <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">south coast of the Australian continent</a> and charted about 1,800 kilometres of it between <a href="/wiki/Cape_Leeuwin" title="Cape Leeuwin">Cape Leeuwin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nuyts_Archipelago" title="Nuyts Archipelago">Nuyts Archipelago</a>.</li>\n<li>1628: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_East_India_Company" title="Portuguese East India Company">Portuguese East India Company</a> (1628\xe2\x80\x931633).</li>\n<li>1629: <a href="/wiki/Wiebbe_Hayes_Stone_Fort" title="Wiebbe Hayes Stone Fort">Wiebbe Hayes Stone Fort</a> (<a href="/wiki/West_Wallabi_Island" title="West Wallabi Island">West Wallabi Island</a>), the first known European structure to be built on the <a href="/wiki/Australian_continent" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian continent">Australian continent</a>. It was built by survivors of the <a href="/wiki/Batavia_(ship)" title="Batavia (ship)">Batavia shipwreck and massacre</a>.</li>\n<li>1636: <a href="/wiki/Lamey_Island_massacre" title="Lamey Island massacre">Lamey Island massacre</a>.</li>\n<li>1636\xe2\x80\x931637: <a href="/wiki/Tulip_Mania" class="mw-redirect" title="Tulip Mania">Tulip Mania</a>, generally considered to be the first recorded <a href="/wiki/Economic_bubble" title="Economic bubble">economic bubble</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Speculative_bubble" class="mw-redirect" title="Speculative bubble">speculative bubble</a>) in history. Early <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_bubble" title="Stock market bubble">stock market bubbles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_crash" title="Stock market crash">crashes</a> also have their roots in financial activities of the Dutch East India Company and Dutch Republic.</li>\n<li>1637: <a href="/wiki/Hansken" title="Hansken">Hansken</a>, a young female <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">Asian elephant</a> from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Dutch Ceylon</a>, was brought to Amsterdam in 1637, aboard a VOC ship. <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Golden_Age_painting" title="Dutch Golden Age painting">Dutch Golden Age artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a> made some historical drawings of Hansken.<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>1638\xe2\x80\x931710: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">Dutch Mauritius</a>, the first permanent <a href="/wiki/Human_settlement" title="Human settlement">human settlement</a> to be established in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mauritius" title="History of Mauritius">Mauritius</a>.</li>\n<li>1640\xe2\x80\x931796: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Ceylon" title="Dutch Ceylon">Dutch Ceylon</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1641\xe2\x80\x931825: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malacca" title="Dutch Malacca">Dutch Malacca</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1641\xe2\x80\x931853: Beginnings of <a href="/wiki/Rangaku" title="Rangaku">Rangaku</a> (first phase: 1641\xe2\x80\x931720). After 1641, the VOC businessmen were the only Western allowed to trade with or to enter <a href="/wiki/Sakoku" title="Sakoku">isolated Japan</a>.</li>\n<li>1642: The VOC explorer <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> discovered, explored, and charted <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> and its neighboring islands. He named Tasmania <a href="/wiki/Anthoonij_van_Diemenslandt" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthoonij van Diemenslandt">Anthoonij van Diemenslandt</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anglicised" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicised">Anglicised</a> as <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen&#39;s Land">Van Diemen\'s Land</a>), after <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Diemen" title="Anthony van Diemen">Anthony van Diemen</a>, the Dutch East India Company\'s Governor General, who had commissioned his voyage.</li>\n<li>1642: On December 13, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>\'s VOC crew were the first non-natives known to discover, explore and chart <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>\'s coastline (<a href="/wiki/Nova_Zeelandia" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Zeelandia">Nova Zeelandia</a>).</li>\n<li>1643: The VOC\'s navigator <a href="/wiki/Maarten_Gerritsz_Vries" title="Maarten Gerritsz Vries">Maarten Gerritsz Vries</a> became the first recorded European to explore and map <a href="/wiki/Vries_Strait" title="Vries Strait">Vries Strait</a>.</li>\n<li>1643: <a href="/wiki/Tr%E1%BB%8Bnh%E2%80%93Nguy%E1%BB%85n_War" title="Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War">Tr\xe1\xbb\x8bnh\xe2\x80\x93Nguy\xe1\xbb\x85n War</a>.</li>\n<li>1643\xe2\x80\x931644: <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Dutch_War" title="Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War">Cambodian\xe2\x80\x93Dutch War</a>.</li>\n<li>1646: <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_La_Naval_de_Manila" title="Battles of La Naval de Manila">Battles of La Naval de Manila</a>.</li>\n<li>1648: <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>.</li>\n<li>1652\xe2\x80\x931654: <a href="/wiki/First_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="First Anglo-Dutch War">First Anglo-Dutch War</a>.</li>\n<li>1652\xe2\x80\x931806: <a href="/wiki/Kaapstad" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaapstad">Kaapstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/History_of_Cape_Town" title="History of Cape Town">Cape Town</a>), the first <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> to be established in <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Africa" title="History of South Africa">South Africa</a>.</li>\n<li>1653\xe2\x80\x931666: The VOC bookkeeper <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Hamel" title="Hendrick Hamel">Hendrick Hamel</a> was the first known non-Asian to experience first-hand and write about <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> (often referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Hermit_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Hermit Kingdom">Hermit Kingdom</a>").</li>\n<li>1659: Beginnings of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_African_wine" title="History of South African wine">South African wine industry</a>.</li>\n<li>1659\xe2\x80\x931677: <a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi%E2%80%93Dutch_Wars" title="Khoikhoi\xe2\x80\x93Dutch Wars">Khoikhoi\xe2\x80\x93Dutch Wars</a>.</li>\n<li>1660: <a href="/wiki/King_Charles_II_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="King Charles II of England">King Charles II of England</a> sailed from <a href="/wiki/Breda" title="Breda">Breda</a> to <a href="/wiki/Delft" title="Delft">Delft</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yacht</a> owned by the VOC. <i><a href="/wiki/HMY_Mary" title="HMY Mary">HMY Mary</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/HMY_Bezan" title="HMY Bezan">HMY Bezan</a></i> (both were built by the VOC) were given to Charles II, <a href="/wiki/Restoration_of_Charles_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Restoration of Charles II">on the restoration of the monarchy</a>, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Gift" title="Dutch Gift">Dutch Gift</a>.</li>\n<li>1661\xe2\x80\x931795: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Malabar" title="Dutch Malabar">Dutch Malabar</a> by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1662: The publication of <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Blaeu" class="mw-redirect" title="Johannes Blaeu">Johannes Blaeu</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Atlas_Maior" title="Atlas Maior">Atlas Maior</a></i> (first edition) in Amsterdam. Johannes Blaeu (also known as <a href="/wiki/Joan_Blaeu" title="Joan Blaeu">Joan Blaeu</a>), like his father <a href="/wiki/Willem_Blaeu" title="Willem Blaeu">Willem Blaeu</a>, was an official cartographer to the VOC. Along with <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius" title="Abraham Ortelius">Abraham Ortelius</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Theatrum_Orbis_Terrarum" title="Theatrum Orbis Terrarum">Theatrum Orbis Terrarum</a></i> (1570), the <i>Atlas Maior</i> (1662\xe2\x80\x9365) is widely considered a masterpiece of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Netherlandish_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography">Golden Age of Netherlandish cartography</a> (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Dutch_cartography" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Dutch cartography">Golden Age of Dutch cartography</a>).</li>\n<li>1664: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a> (1664\xe2\x80\x931794).</li>\n<li>1665\xe2\x80\x931667: <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a>.</li>\n<li>1665: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_V%C3%A5gen" title="Battle of V\xc3\xa5gen">Battle of V\xc3\xa5gen</a>, in August 1665 as part of the Second Anglo-Dutch War.</li>\n<li>1666\xe2\x80\x931679: The <a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Good_Hope" title="Castle of Good Hope">Castle of Good Hope</a>, the oldest surviving building in South Africa, was built by the VOC.</li>\n<li>1672\xe2\x80\x931674: <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a>.</li>\n<li>1672\xe2\x80\x931678: <a href="/wiki/Franco-Dutch_War" title="Franco-Dutch War">Franco-Dutch War</a>.</li>\n<li>1679: <a href="/wiki/Stellenbosch" title="Stellenbosch">Stellenbosch</a>, the second oldest urban area (town) in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, was founded in 1679 by the Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Dutch Cape Colony</a> <a href="/wiki/Simon_van_der_Stel" title="Simon van der Stel">Simon van der Stel</a>.</li>\n<li>1680: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Simonstad" class="mw-redirect" title="Simonstad">Simonstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/Simon%27s_Town" title="Simon&#39;s Town">Simon\'s Town</a>), a town near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>.</li>\n<li>1688\xe2\x80\x931689: The first large-scale <a href="/wiki/Huguenots_in_South_Africa" title="Huguenots in South Africa">emigration of Huguenots</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony" title="Dutch Cape Colony">Dutch Cape Colony</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>).</li>\n<li>1688: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Franschhoek" title="Franschhoek">Franschhoek</a>, a town in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Cape Province">Western Cape Province</a>, in 1688 <a href="/wiki/Huguenots_in_South_Africa" title="Huguenots in South Africa">by Huguenots</a>.</li>\n<li>1688: After observing and analyzing the workings of the VOC-lead Dutch stock market, Amsterdam-based businessman <a href="/wiki/Joseph_de_la_Vega" title="Joseph de la Vega">Joseph de la Vega</a> published <i>Confusion de Confusiones</i>, the earliest known book about <a href="/wiki/Stock_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock trading">stock trading</a> and first book on the inner workings of the <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>) in its modern sense. The publication of <i>Confusion de Confusiones</i> (1688) helped lay the foundations for modern fields of <a href="/wiki/Technical_analysis" title="Technical analysis">technical analysis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_finance" class="mw-redirect" title="Behavioral finance">behavioral finance</a>.</li>\n<li>1697: European discovery of <a href="/wiki/Black_swan" title="Black swan">black swans</a> for the first time in history, by the VOC navigator <a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Vlamingh" title="Willem de Vlamingh">Willem de Vlamingh</a>.</li>\n<li>1697: In his undercover visit to the Dutch Republic as part of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Embassy_of_Peter_the_Great" title="Grand Embassy of Peter the Great">Grand Embassy mission</a> (1697\xe2\x80\x9398), Tsar <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter I of Russia">Peter I of Russia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>) worked incognito as a <a href="/wiki/Shipwright" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipwright">ship\'s carpenter</a> at the VOC\'s shipyards in Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a>/<a href="/wiki/Saardam" class="mw-redirect" title="Saardam">Saardam</a>, for a period of four months.</li>\n<li>1704\xe2\x80\x931708: <a href="/wiki/First_Javanese_War_of_Succession" title="First Javanese War of Succession">First Javanese War of Succession</a>.</li>\n<li>1712: The wreck of VOC ship <i><a href="/wiki/Zuytdorp" title="Zuytdorp">Zuytdorp</a></i> on the Western Australian coast.</li>\n<li>1719\xe2\x80\x931723: <a href="/wiki/Second_Javanese_War_of_Succession" title="Second Javanese War of Succession">Second Javanese War of Succession</a>.</li>\n<li>1722: In the service of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> (WIC/GWIC), Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Roggeveen" title="Jacob Roggeveen">Jacob Roggeveen</a> and his crew were arrested for violating the monopoly of the VOC and sent back to the Dutch Republic almost as prisoners on ships of the VOC, the rivals of the Dutch West India Company.</li>\n<li>1731: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">Swedish East India Company</a> (1731\xe2\x80\x931813).</li>\n<li>1740: <a href="/wiki/1740_Batavia_massacre" title="1740 Batavia massacre">Batavia massacre</a>.</li>\n<li>1746: Establishment of <a href="/wiki/Swellendam" title="Swellendam">Swellendam</a>, the third oldest urban area (town) in South Africa.</li>\n<li>1749\xe2\x80\x931757: <a href="/wiki/Third_Javanese_War_of_Succession" title="Third Javanese War of Succession">Third Javanese War of Succession</a>.</li>\n<li>1766: <a href="/wiki/Meermin_slave_mutiny" title="Meermin slave mutiny"><i>Meermin</i> slave mutiny</a>.</li>\n<li>1780\xe2\x80\x931784: <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Dutch War">Fourth Anglo-Dutch War</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
